Exception of Building from House in Acknowledgment
Ruling on the exception of the building from a house in acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's ruling on excepting the building in an acknowledgment and explain the qiyas from sale that supports it.

Core Idea
Excepting the building is invalid because the building is an inseparable part of the house.

When someone acknowledges a house but tries to except the building, a legal question arises: does the exception work? In this lesson, we examine Abu Hanifa's position that the building is included as a dependent part, supported by an analogy to the rules of sale. We also explore the dissent of the three imams and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
The case: a person says 'This house is for Zaid except the building.' According to Abu Hanifa, the exception is invalid, so the entire house including the building belongs to Zaid.
2
Understand the rationale
The building is linguistically and legally a part of the house; the word 'house' includes the building. An exception is a verbal manipulation that does not change the reality.
3
Trace the proof from sale
The proof comes from the chapter of sale: when a house is sold, the building is included as a dependent part (tābi‘). If the building is later found to belong to someone else, the buyer does not get a price reduction but can cancel the sale. This shows the building is inseparable.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The three imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Zufar) hold that the exception is valid and the building goes to the excepting party. Their view aligns with the Shafi'i school.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استثنى البناء من الدار فهما للمقر له (فتح) من الدار: بأن قال: هذه الدار لزيد والبناء لنفسي. (عيني) فهما للمقر له: لأن البناء داخل في الإقرار بالدار معنى لفظاً، والاستثناء تصرف في اللفظ فلم يصح، وعند الثلاثة: يصح فلا يكون البناء له. (عيني)] والدليل على هذا فصل البيع، فإن البناء في بيع الدار يدخل تحت البيع تبعاً، حتى لو استحق البناء قبل القبض لا يسقط شيء من الثمن بمقابلته، بل يخير المشتري، بخلاف ما إذا قال: "إلا ثلثها أو إلا بيتاً فيها"، حيث يصح الاستثناء، ويكون للمقر له ما عدا ثلث الدار، وما سوى هذا البيت؛ لأن البيت في لفظ الدار دخل مقصوداً، حتى لو استحق البيت في بيع الدار سقط حصته من الثمن، ولا يصح استثناء البناء كالثلث والبيت باعتبار أنه جزء الدار؛ لأنه زائد بمعنى أن اسم الدار لا ينتفي بانتفائه. (عيني، فتح، (كفاية والعرصة وهي ) البقعة الخالية عن الشجر والبناء. (ط)

كتاب الإقرار
۵۹
الاستثناء وما في معناه
فكما قال [ أي حكم إقراره مثل ما قال المقر، فيكون بناء الدار للمقر وصحنها للمخاطب.(محشي)] أي يكون البناء له، والعرصة للمقر له؛ لأن العرصة اسم للبقعة الخالية عن البناء والشجر، فيكون مقراً ببياض هذه الأرض دون البناء، بخلاف ما إذا قال مكان "العرصة": "الأرض" بأن قال: "بناء هذه الدار لي وأرضها لفلان"، حيث يكون البناء أيضاً لفلان؛ لأن الأرض كالدار فيتبعها البناء، وإذا قال: "بناء هذه الدار لزيد والأرض لعمرو"، حيث يكون لكل واحد منهما ما أقر به ولو قدم الإقرار بالأرض، كان الكل للمقر له؛ لأن البناء تبع للأرض، والأصل: أن دعواه لنفسه لا تمنع الإقرار لغيره، وإقراره لا يقبل على غيره. (عيني، فتح)
And if he excepts the building from the house, then both belong to the one acknowledged to. (Commentary:) The building is included in the acknowledgment of the house by meaning and wording, so the exception is an invalid manipulation of the wording. According to the three imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar?), it is valid and the building is not for him. The evidence for this is the chapter of sale: in the sale of a house, the building is included as a follow-up; if the building is seized before delivery, no part of the price is reduced, unlike if he said 'except one-third' or 'except a room' which is valid. The 'arsa (courtyard) is empty land without trees or building. If he says 'the building is mine and the arsa is yours', the building is for him and the arsa for the addressee. If he says 'the ground (ard) instead of arsa', the building also goes to the latter because the ground, like the house, includes the building.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage deals with the exception of the building when acknowledging a house. The author rules that the exception is invalid, so both the house and the building go to the person acknowledged to (al-muqarr lahu). The commentary explains that the building is linguistically and legally part of the house; an exception is a verbal manipulation that cannot change the reality. The proof is from the rules of sale: in selling a house, the building is included automatically as a dependent part (tābi‘). If the building is later found to be owned by another, the buyer does not get a refund for the building separately; rather, he has the option to cancel the sale. This contrasts with excepting a specific room or one-third, which is valid because those are independent parts that can be separated. The commentary also distinguishes between 'arsa (courtyard) and 'ard (land); acknowledging the land includes the building, whereas acknowledging the courtyard does not. The discussion includes the opinions of the three imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar) who consider the exception valid, meaning the building belongs to the person making the exception.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā’): An exception clause in an acknowledgment, specifically excepting a part of what is acknowledged.
تبعاً (taba‘an): As a dependent or subsidiary part; the building is included as a follow-up to the house.
عرصة (‘arṣa): Courtyard or empty land without trees or buildings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'This house is for Zaid except the building,' according to Abu Hanifa, who owns the building?
A) The person making the acknowledgment (al-muqirr).
B) Zaid (al-muqarr lahu).
C) The building is not owned by anyone.
D) It depends on whether the building is attached or not.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the building is an inseparable part of the house, so an exception of the building in an acknowledgment is invalid and the building goes to the person acknowledged to.

Acknowledging Debt from the Price of a Slave Not Yet Delivered
Detailed cases of acknowledgment of debt from the price of a slave with pending delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four scenarios of acknowledging a debt from the price of a slave and apply the Hanafi ruling for each, including the intra-Hanafi difference regarding specification.

Core Idea
An acknowledgment of debt from the price of a slave is conditional on delivery only if the slave is specified; otherwise, the debt is absolute and non-delivery claims are not accepted.

This passage presents a detailed set of legal scenarios concerning an acknowledgment (iqrar) of a debt of one thousand dirhams arising from the price of a slave. The central question is whether the debtor's claim that he has not taken delivery of the slave affects his obligation to pay. The ruling depends critically on whether the slave is specified (mu‘ayyan) or unspecified, and on whether the debtor's statement about non-delivery is connected or disconnected to the acknowledgment. We will explore four possible disputes between the debtor and creditor and the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two leading students on the unspecified case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main branches of the ruling
The passage divides the cases based on whether the slave is specified or unspecified. Determine which branch a given scenario falls into first.
Specification means the debtor identifies a particular slave (e.g., 'this slave' or points to one).
2
Analyze the specified slave case
If the slave is specified, the acknowledgment is conditional on its delivery. Without delivery, the debt is not due. Study the four sub-scenarios (their agreements/disagreements) and the outcome of each.
The four sub-scenarios involve different claims by the creditor about ownership and the slave's identity.
3
Analyze the unspecified slave case
If the slave is not specified, the ruling differs between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Distinguish between connected and disconnected statements.
This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf hinges on whether the debtor's claim of non-delivery is a retraction or a permissible explanation.
4
Apply the rulings to new scenarios
Given a scenario with a similar fact pattern, determine the applicable branch and state the ruling, citing the relevant principle (specification, connection).
Practice with examples involving other objects (e.g., a car) to test understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن عين: بأن ذكر عبداً بعينه أو قال: من ثمن هذا العبد (عيني) لزمه الألف: أي لو قال رجل: "علي ألف لفلان من ثمن عبد اشتريته منه، و لم أقبضه وذكر ذلك موصولاً بإقراره، فإن عين العبد بأن ذكر عبداً بعينه، أو أشار إلى معين، لزم المشتري المقر الألف؛ لأنه أقر بالألف على صفة، وهي سلامة العبد له، فلما سلم المقر له العبد إليه وجد الصفة التي أقر بها. وإلا لا أي وإن لم يسلم المقر له العبد إلى المشتري لا شيء له على المقر؛ لأن الصفة التي أقر بها لم توجد ولا تلزمه بدونها. وهذه المسألة على وجوه أحدها: هذا، وهو ما إذا صدقه وسلمه إليه وحكمه لزوم الألف؛ لأن الثابت بتصادقهما كالثابت عياناً. والثاني: أن يقول المقر له: "العبد عبدك ما بعتكه، وإنما بعتك غيره وقد قبضته، ولي عليك ألف درهم ثمنه"، وفيه المال لازم على المقر؛ لأنهما اتفقا على ما أقرا به واختلفا في سببه، ولا عبرة لاختلاف السبب عند حصول المقصود واتحاد الحكم. والثالث: أن يقول: العبد عبدي ما بعتكه"، وفيه لا يلزم شيء على المقر؛ لعدم سلامة العبد له. والرابع أن يقول: "العبد عبدي ما بعتكه، وإنما بعتك غيره"، وحكمه: أن يتحالفا، وإذا تحالفا انتفى دعوى كل واحد منهما عن صاحبه، فلا يقضى عليه بشيء من المال، والعبد سالم لمن في يده، وجه التحالف: أن كلاً منهما مدع ومنكر؛ لأن المقر يدعي تسليم من عينه، والآخر ينكر، والمقر له يدعي على المقر أيضاً ببيع غيره، وهو ينكر. (عيني، فتح) وإن لم يعين أي المقر العبد بأن قال: "علي" ألف من ثمن "عبد. (معدن) لزمه الألف ولا يصدق في قوله: "ما قبضته" وصل كلامه أو فصل. (عيني)] أي مطلقاً سواء وصل أو فصل، ولا يصدق في قوله: "لم أقبضه" عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه رجوع عن الإقرار؛ لأن الصدر موجب، وإنكار قبض مبيع غير معين ينافيه، وعندهما: إن وصل صدق؛ لأنه بيان تغيير، فصح موصولاً لا مفصولاً كالاستثناء والشرط، فلا يلزمه شيء، وإن فصل لم يصدق إذا أنكر المقر له أن يكون ذلك من ثمن العبد ولزمه ألف وإن أقر أنه من ثمن العبد فالقول قول المقر: إني لم أقبضه؛ لأن البيع لما ثبت بتصادقهما بقي أمر القبض مجملاً؛ لأنه لم يقر به نصاً ولا اقتضاء، وإقراره بوجوب الثمن ليس إقرارا
If he specifies: by mentioning a particular slave or saying 'from the price of this slave', the one thousand dirhams are binding. ... If the slave is delivered, the debt is due; if not delivered, nothing is due. The issue has several aspects: first, if he affirms and delivers, the debt is due. Second, if the creditor says 'the slave is yours, I did not sell it to you, but sold you another and you received it', the money is still binding. Third, if he says 'the slave is mine, I did not sell it to you', nothing is due. Fourth, if the two parties contradict and take oaths, no payment is ordered. If the slave is not specified, the one thousand dirhams are due and the debtor is not believed in saying he did not receive it, according to Abu Hanifa, whether he says it connected or disconnected; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if he says it connected, he is believed and nothing is due; if disconnected, he is not believed.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed set of cases regarding an acknowledgment of a debt of one thousand dirhams from the price of a slave that the debtor claims he has not yet taken delivery of. The key distinction is whether the slave is specified (mu‘ayyan) or not. If specified, the debt becomes due only upon delivery of that specific slave to the debtor; if not delivered, no debt is owed because the acknowledgment was conditional on delivery. The text enumerates four possible scenarios: (1) Both agree and the slave is delivered: debt due. (2) The creditor says the slave belongs to the debtor but no sale occurred; still debt due because they agree on the debt. (3) The creditor denies any sale and claims the slave is his; no debt due. (4) Mutual contradiction leads to oaths (tahāluf) and no debt, with the slave remaining in the possessor's hands. If the slave is not specified, the ruling differs: according to Abu Hanifa, the acknowledgment is absolute and the debtor cannot later claim non-delivery; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if he says it connected (muttaṣil) to the acknowledgment, he is believed; if said separately (munfaṣil), he is not believed.

Key Terms
عين (‘ayyin): To specify or designate a particular item (here, a specific slave).
موصولاً (mawṣūlan): Connected; when the debtor's statement about non-delivery is immediately linked to the acknowledgment in one utterance.
تحالف (taḥāluf): Mutual oaths taken by both parties when they contradict each other in contract disputes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone acknowledges owing 1000 dirhams from the price of a slave but does not specify the slave, and later claims he never received the slave, what is the ruling?
A) He is believed and does not have to pay.
B) He is not believed and must pay the 1000 dirhams.
C) The case is decided by mutual oaths.
D) He only pays if the slave is delivered later.

Key Takeaway
The bindingness of an acknowledgment of debt from the price of a slave depends critically on whether the slave is specified and, if unspecified, on whether the claim of non-delivery is connected and on which Hanafi view is followed.

Exception of Quantity in Acknowledgment
Rulings on exception of quantity and description in acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on excepting a quantity in an acknowledgment and identify when such an exception is accepted.

Core Idea
An exception of quantity in acknowledgment is valid only if connected; an exception of description is never valid.

In Hanafi law, when someone acknowledges a debt, they may add an exception like 'except that it lacks so much.' The ruling hinges on whether the exception is made immediately after the acknowledgment (connected) or later (disconnected). This lesson also covers the special case of describing dirhams as counterfeit and the dispensation for necessity breaks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its effect
Determine what is being ruled upon: the acknowledgment (iqrar) with an exception of a specific quantity.
The ruling is about whether the exception is believed (yusaddaq) or not.
2
Distinguish exception of quantity vs. description
Note that exception of quantity (e.g., 'except that it lacks five dirhams') is valid if connected, but exception of description (e.g., 'counterfeit') is not valid even if connected.
The basis: quantity exception is a modifying explanation (bayān mughayyir) that changes the amount; description does not change the amount.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement on counterfeit dirhams
If someone says 'So-and-so owes me a thousand dirhams, counterfeit' without mentioning a sale or loan, Abu Hanifa says he must pay good dirhams regardless; the Sahibayn say if connected he is believed, if disconnected not.
This shows the principle: connected exception of amount is accepted; disconnected or description is not.
4
Understand the dispensation for necessity
If a break occurs due to breath, cough, or someone holding his mouth, Abu Yusuf rules it is considered connected to avoid hardship, and this is the fatwa.
Necessity (ḥaraj) allows flexibility in the connection requirement.
5
Summarize the final ruling
State the mufta bihi: connected exception of quantity is accepted; disconnected is not; exception of description is never accepted; breaks due to necessity are excused.
This ruling applies to all contracts where acknowledgment occurs (sale, loan, usurpation, deposit).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال: "إلا أنه ينقص كذا متصلا صدق وإلا لا، ومن أقر بغصب ثوب وجاء بمعيب صدق، وإن قال: أخذت منك ألفا وديعة وهلكت، وقال: أخذتها غصبا، فهو ضامن، وإن قال : أعطيتنيها وديعة وقال غصبتنيها لا يضمن. ولو قال: "الفلان" علي ألف درهم زيوف" فقط بدون ذكر البيع والقرض، قيل: يصدق إجماعاً إذا وصل، وقيل: هو على الخلاف أيضاً، لا يصدق عنده ويلزمه الجياد، وعندهما: إن وصل صدق وإن فصل لا. (فتح، عناية) ولو قال أي المقر الفلان" على ألف درهم ( عيني) متصلا أي حال كون ذلك المقدار المستثنى متصلا بكلامه. (عيني) صدق : أي لو قال في البيع والغصب والقرض والوديعة إن لفلان" علي ألفا إلا أنه ينقص كذا"، وقال بالاستثناء موصولاً صدق المقر؛ لأنه استثنى القدر فيكون بيان تغيير، ويصح استثناء القدر موصولا لا استثناء الوصف كالزيافة وإلا لا أي وإن لم يقل الاستثناء متصلاً بل قاله منفصلاً لا يصدق؛ لأن بيان التغيير لا مفصولاً. يصح ثم اعلم أنه لو وقع الفصل بين الاستثناء وبين صدره ضرورة انقطاع الكلام بانقطاع النفس، أو بسبب دفع سعال، أو بإمساك أحد فمه، فعن أبي دفعاً للحرج، وبه يفتى؛ لأن الإنسان يحتاج إلى أن يتكلم كثيراً ويذكر الاستثناء في آخره، ولا يمكنه أن يتكلم بجميع ذلك بنفس واحد، فكان يوسف: أنه وصل عفواً. (عيني فتح كفاية صدق لأن الغصب لا يختص بالسليم من العيوب كالوديعة. (عيني) وهلكت أي وقد هلكت الألف عندي فهو ضامن: لأن المقر أقر بسبب الضمان وهو الأخذ ومثله القبض، ثم ادعى ما يوجب البراءة، وهو الإذن بالأخذ، والآخر منكر، فالقول قوله مع يمينه، بخلاف ما إذا قال المقر له: بل أخذتها قرضاً، حيث يكون القول للمقر؛ لأنهما تصادقا على أن الأخذ حصل بإذنه، وهذا لا يوجب الضمان على الآخذ إلا باعتبار عقد الضمان فالمالك يدعي عليه العقد، وهو ينكر ، فالقول قول المنكر. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٢٤/٢] وعلى هذا إذا أقر بأخذ الثوب وديعة وقال المقر له بل أخذته بيعاً كان القول للمقر، وفي مسألة الكتاب القول قول المقر له مع يمينه، وإن نكل عن يمينه لا يضمن المقر، والدليل على كون الأخذ سببا للضمان قوله عليه : على اليد ما أخذت حتى ترده". (فتح، كفاية) وديعة: أي لأجل كونها وديعة عندي فهلكت عيني غصبتنيها : أي لو قال رجل: "أعطيتني ألف درهم؛ لأجل كونها وديعة عندي فهلكت، وقال المالك: ليس كذلك، بل غصبت الألف المذكور مني، لا يضمن المقر؛ إذ لم يقر الضمان، بل بالإعطاء وهو فعل المقر له وهو يدعي على المقر سبب الضمان، والمقر ينكره، فالقول قول المقر، والحاصل أن المقر إما أن يتكلم بما يدل على فعل نفسه كقوله: "أخذت" ونحوه، أو على فعل غيره كـ"أعطيتني؟، فإن كان الأول وأتى بما لا يوجب الضمان نحو أن يقول: "أخذت وديعة"، فإن صدقه المقر له فذلك، وإن كذبه، فإن ادعى ما يدل على الإذن بالأخذ كالقرض، فالقول للمقر مع يمينه وإن ادعى غيره ضمن المقر؛ بسبب
And if he said: 'except that it lacks so much' connected, he is believed, otherwise not. And whoever acknowledges the usurpation of a garment and comes with a defective one is believed. And if he said: 'I took from you a thousand as a deposit and it was destroyed', and he said: 'I took it as a usurpation', then he is liable. And if he said: 'You gave it to me as a deposit' and he said 'You usurped it from me', he is not liable. And if he said: 'So-and-so owes me a thousand dirhams, counterfeit' only without mentioning the sale or loan, it is said: he is believed by consensus if connected, and it is said: it is also upon the disagreement: he is not believed according to him (Abu Hanifa) and the good dirhams are binding on him, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): if connected he is believed, if disconnected then not. (Fath, Inayah) And if the acknowledging person said: 'So-and-so owes me a thousand dirhams' (Ayni) connected, i.e., while that excepted amount is connected to his speech. (Ayni) He is believed: i.e., if he said in sale, usurpation, loan, and deposit: 'So-and-so owes me a thousand except that it lacks so much', and he said the exception connectedly, the acknowledging person is believed; because he excepted the amount, so it becomes a modifying explanation, and exception of an amount is valid connectedly, not exception of a description like counterfeitness. Otherwise, i.e., if he did not say the exception connectedly but said it separately, he is not believed; because a modifying explanation is not valid separately. Then know that if a separation occurs between the exception and its beginning due to necessity of interruption of speech by breath, or due to coughing, or someone holding his mouth, it is reported from Abu Yusuf that it is considered connected, out of hardship, and this is the relied-upon fatwa; because a person needs to speak a lot and mention the exception at the end, and he cannot say all that in one breath. (Ayni, Fath, Kifayah) He is believed because usurpation is not specific to soundness from defects, like deposit. (Ayni) And it was destroyed: i.e., and the thousand has been destroyed with him, so he is liable: because the acknowledging person acknowledged the cause of liability, which is taking and like it receiving, then he claimed what necessitates exoneration, which is permission to take, and the other denies, so the statement is his with his oath. Contrary to if the acknowledgee said: 'Rather you took it as a loan', where the statement is of the acknowledging person; because they agree that the taking occurred with his permission, and this does not impose liability on the taker except by consideration of the contract of liability, so the owner claims a contract against him and he denies, so the statement is of the denier. [Risala: 224/2] And upon this, if he acknowledged taking a garment as a deposit and the acknowledgee said: 'Rather you took it as a sale', the statement is of the acknowledging person. And in the issue of the book, the statement is of the acknowledgee with his oath, and if he declines his oath, the acknowledging person is not liable. And the evidence that taking is a cause of liability is his statement (peace be upon him): 'The hand is liable for what it has taken until it returns it.' (Fath, Kifayah) Deposit: i.e., because it was a deposit with me and it was destroyed. (Ayni) 'You usurped it from me': i.e., if a man said: 'You gave me a thousand dirhams, because it was a deposit with me and it was destroyed', and the owner said: 'It is not so, rather you usurped the mentioned thousand from me', the acknowledging person is not liable; because he did not acknowledge liability, but rather acknowledged giving, which is an act of the acknowledgee, and he (the acknowledgee) claims a cause of liability against the acknowledging person, and the acknowledging person denies it, so the statement is of the acknowledging person. The summary: the acknowledging person either speaks of his own act like his saying 'I took' and the like, or of the act of another like 'you gave me'. If it is the first and he brings something that does not impose liability, like saying 'I took as a deposit', if the acknowledgee believes him then that is it, and if he denies him, then if he claims something that indicates permission to take like loan, the statement is of the acknowledging person with his oath, and if he claims something else, the acknowledging person is liable.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings on acknowledgment (iqrar) related to exception of quantity and disputes over the nature of a taking (deposit vs. usurpation). It is a ruling with proof. The first part deals with an exception of a specific amount (e.g., 'except that it lacks so much'): if stated connectedly, the debtor is believed; if disconnected, not. This is because excepting an amount is a modifying explanation (bayān mughayyir) and is valid only when connected, unlike an exception of a description (like counterfeitness) which is not valid even when connected. An exception is allowed for necessity (like interruption of speech) due to hardship, and this is the fatwa. The second part addresses acknowledging the usurpation (ghaṣb) of a garment that is defective: the acknowledging person is believed because usurpation does not require soundness. The third part is about a person who says he took a thousand dirhams as a deposit and they were destroyed; if the owner claims it was usurpation, the taker is liable because he acknowledged the taking (a cause of liability) and then claims a defense (permission), but the owner denies. However, if the owner claims it was a loan, the taker's statement is accepted because both agree the taking was with permission. The principle is that the acknowledging person's admission of taking creates a presumption of liability; his claim of a trust (amāna) is a defense he must prove. The hadith 'The hand is liable for what it has taken until it returns it' is cited as evidence. The passage also discusses the case where the taker says 'you gave me' (i.e., the owner gave him) as a deposit; then the taker does not acknowledge liability because the act is attributed to the owner. The ruling depends on whether the taker speaks of his own act (taking) or the other's act (giving). The passage ends with a summary: if the taker says 'I took as a deposit', and the owner denies it, the owner's statement is taken with his oath; if the owner claims loan, the taker is believed because that implies permission to take; if the owner claims usurpation, the taker is liable because he acknowledged the taking without permission.

Key Terms
استثناء القدر (istithnā’ al-qadr): Exception of a specific quantity (e.g., 'except that it lacks so much').
بيان تغيير (bayān mughayyir): A modifying explanation that changes the initial ruling.
زيوف (zuyūf): Counterfeit dirhams (defective currency).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A debtor says: 'I owe you 1000 dirhams' and then immediately says 'except they are counterfeit.' According to the Sahibayn, what is the ruling?
A) He is believed and only owes counterfeit dirhams.
B) He is not believed and must pay good dirhams.
C) The acknowledgment is void.
D) He must pay 1000 dirhams of any type.

Key Takeaway
The exception of a specific quantity in an acknowledgment is accepted only if connected; an exception of a description (like counterfeitness) is not accepted even if connected, except where necessity excuses a break.

Acknowledgment of Taking: Deposit vs. Usurpation
Rulings on liability in disputes over deposit, usurpation, and defective goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine liability based on how a person acknowledges taking property and distinguish between cases where the taker is liable or not.

Core Idea
Acknowledging a taking creates a presumption of liability unless the taker claims a basis of permission (like loan) or the owner's own act (like giving).

When someone admits taking another's property, the nature of that taking determines liability. If the taker says 'I took as a deposit' but the owner says 'you usurped it', the taker is liable because he admitted the taking (a cause of liability) and his claim of deposit is a defense he must prove. However, if the taker says 'you gave me as a deposit', the act is attributed to the owner, and the taker is not liable. This lesson also covers the case of acknowledging a defective garment in usurpation and the hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key scenarios
There are three main scenarios: (1) Acknowledgment of usurpation of a defective garment – he is believed because usurpation does not require soundness. (2) Taker says 'I took as a deposit' – owner says 'usurpation' – taker is liable. (3) Taker says 'you gave me as a deposit' – owner says 'usurpation' – taker is not liable.
The distinction hinges on whether the taker speaks of his own act (taking) or the owner's act (giving).
2
Understand the principle of cause of liability
The hadith 'The hand is liable for what it has taken until it returns it' shows that taking (akhdh) is itself a cause of liability (ḍamān). The taker must return the property or compensate.
This is a zanni (speculative) proof but binding in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the 'I took as deposit' case
The taker admits taking (cause of liability) but then claims he had permission (deposit). Since the owner denies permission, the taker's claim is a defense; the taker is liable because he cannot prove permission.
Contrast with the 'I took as loan' case where the owner claims loan – both agree taking was with permission, so the taker is not liable (owner's claim of contract is disputed).
4
Analyze the 'you gave me as deposit' case
Here the taker attributes the act to the owner (giving), not his own taking. He does not admit liability; the owner's claim of usurpation is an assertion of a cause of liability against the taker, which the taker denies. The taker's statement is accepted with his oath.
The rule: if the taker's wording does not admit liability, he is not liable unless the owner proves usurpation.
5
Apply to the defective garment case
If someone acknowledges usurping a garment and then returns a defective one, he is believed (i.e., his claim that it was defective when taken is accepted) because usurpation does not require the property to be sound; liability is for the value of the property as taken.
This is similar to deposit: the depositary is not liable for pre-existing defects.

Key Terms
غصب (ghaṣb): Usurpation or wrongful taking of another's property without permission.
وديعة (wadī‘a): Deposit (trust) where the depositary holds property for safekeeping without liability for loss unless negligent.
ضامن (ḍāmin): Liable or responsible for compensation.
على اليد ما أخذت حتى ترده (alā al-yad mā akhadhat ḥattā taruddahu): Hadith: 'The hand is liable for what it has taken until it returns it.'

Checkpoint
A says to B: 'You gave me 1000 dirhams as a deposit and it was destroyed.' B says: 'I did not give it; you stole it.' What is the ruling?
A) A is liable because he had the money.
B) A is not liable because he attributes the act to B.
C) Both are liable equally.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
Liability for property loss hinges on whether the possessor admits taking (cause) or attributes the act to the owner; the hadith establishes that taking itself is a cause of liability.

Confession of Taking a Trust: When Possession Implies Liability
Ruling on a taker of a trust who claims it as his own

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a confessor who admits taking a trust and claims ownership, and distinguish between trust hand and liability hand in ijarah disputes.

Core Idea
A confessor's admission of taking creates liability unless the hand is merely functional.

This passage from Kitab al-Iqrar presents rulings on two key scenarios: a person who confesses to taking a trust (wadi'a) and then claims it as his own, and a dispute over ownership after an ijarah contract. The central issue is the nature of the hand (yad) – whether it implies liability or is merely a trust hand. The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, uses istihsan in ijarah to uphold the lessor's claim, while the Sahibayn follow qiyas. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling on trust confession
When a person confesses to taking a trust (wadi'a) and then claims ownership, the confessor must return the object if it exists, otherwise pay its value. This is because the admission of taking establishes a cause for liability.
The act is a confession (iqrar) against oneself, which is conclusive.
2
Analyze the two sub-scenarios for trust
If the confessor adds a claim of liability (e.g., 'I took it as a loan'), and the opponent denies, the opponent's statement is accepted. If the confessor denies liability (e.g., 'You gave me a trust') and the opponent claims usurpation, the confessor's statement is accepted.
The burden of proof shifts based on who asserts a cause of guarantee.
3
Examine the ijarah dispute and the istihsan vs. qiyas
In ijarah, if the lessor claims the item is his after the lessee used and returned it, Abu Hanifa (istihsan) accepts the lessor's statement. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (qiyas) accept the lessee's statement, arguing that the lessor admitted to the lessee's hand.
The hand in ijarah is functional (for usufruct), not possessive.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa's view, the lessor can recover the item; under the Sahibayn's view, the lessee keeps it unless the lessor has evidence.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما في معناه لا، وإن قال: هذا كان وديعة لي عندك فأخذته فقال: هو لي، أخذه، وإن قال: زيد مثلا لعمرو الشيء منك عمرو كذبت س م ف ك د آجرت بعيري أو ثوبي هذا فلانا، فركبه أو لبسه ،فرده فالقول للمقر الخصم سبب قلنا: هو أي إبلي الضمان فركب فلان البعير لبس فلان الثوب 6 أي رجل - لأنهما في الأولى توافقا على أن الأخذ كان بالإذن، والمقر له يدعي سبب الضمان وهو القرض والآخر ينكره، فكان القول قول الآخر، بخلاف الثانية، وإن كان الثاني نحو أن يقول: "أعطيتني وديعة" وادعى الآخر غصباً لم يضمن. والفرق: أنه في الأول أقر بسبب الضمان وادعى ما يبرئه، وأنكر الخصم فكان القول قول الخصم، وفي الثاني ادعى وهو الغصب والمقر منكر، فالقول قول المقر، فإن قيل: إعطاؤه يكون بقبضه فكان مقراً به، قد يكون بالتخلية، والوضع بين يديه، ولو اقتضى ذلك فالمقتضى لا عموم له؛ لثبوته ضرورة، فيقدر بقدرها، فلا يظهر في انعقاده سبباً للضمان فإن نكل المقر عن اليمين يلزمه الألف. (عيني، فتح، عناية) أخذه [ أي عمرو لو قائماً، وإلا فقيمته (عيني] أي لو أقر زيد لعمرو: "أن هذا الشيء كان وديعة لي عندك فأخذته منك"، فقال عمرو: "ليس كذلك بل هذا الشيء لي"، أخذه عمرو ؛ لأن الآخذ المقر أقر باليد لعمرو، ثم بالأخذ منه، وهو سبب الضمان ثم ادعى استحقاقه عليه، فلا يقبل دعواه، فوجب عليه رد العين إن كان قائماً، وإن لم يكن قائما . عليه رد قيمته. رمز الحقائق: ٢٢٥/٢] (فتح) وجب مني فرده أي فرد فلان البعير أو الثوب عليّ، وقال فلان: كذبت" بل البعير والثوب لي". (عيني) فالقول للمقر: أي لو قال رجل: "آجرت بعيري أو ثوبي هذا فلاناً، فركب فلان البعير أو لبس فلان الثوب فرده علي"، وقال فلان: كذبت، بل الثوب والدابة لي، وقد أخذتهما ظلماً"، فالقول للمقر وللآخر البينة، ولو قال: "قبضت منه ألفاً كانت لي عليه، وأنكر" ، فله أخذها؛ لأنه أقر له بالملك وأنه أخذه بحقه وادعى ما يبرئه والآخر ينكر، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة استحساناً وقالا القول للذي أخذ الثوب منه أو الدابة، وهو القياس وبه قالت الثلاثة، وعلى هذا الخلاف العارية والإسكان بأن قال: أعرت فلاناً ،ثوبي ثم أخذته منه، أو أسكنت فلاناً داري ثم أخذتها منه، وقال فلان: هو لي. وجه القياس: أنه أقر باليد له ثم ادعى عليه الاستحقاق فيقبل إقراره له دون دعواه، فيجب عليه الرد، وجه الاستحسان: أن اليد في الإجارة تثبت ضرورة استيفاء المعقود عليه، وهو المنافع، فيكون عدماً في ما وراء الضرورة، فلا يكون إقراراً باليد مقصوداً، فلا يظهر في حق الاستحقاق على المقر، وفي "الإسرار": الاختلاف فيما إذا لم تكن الدابة معروفة للمقر وإلا فالقول قوله بالإجماع؛ لأن الملك فيه معروف للمقر، وهذا يبتني على ما عليه المتقدمون من أن للقاضي القضاء بعلمه وإن كان المفتى به ما ذكره المتأخرون من أ أنه ليس له ذلك، ولوقال: إن فلاناً وزع . هذه الأرض، أو بني هذه الدار، أو غرس هذا الكرم، وذلك كله في يد المقر، وقال المقر له: الملك ملكي، وفعلت ذلك لنفسي، وقال المقر: لا، بل استعنت بك ففعلت، أو فعلته بأجر، كان القول للمقر؛
And what is in its meaning, no. And if he said: 'This was a trust with me when you [took it]' and he said: 'It is mine', he takes it. And if he said: 'Zayd for example, the thing from you, Amr, you lied.' ... And if he said: 'I hired my camel or this cloth of mine to so-and-so, so he rode it or wore it, then he returned it,' then the statement is of the confessor. The opponent is a cause. We said: it is, i.e., my camels, the guarantee. So so-and-so rode the camel, so-and-so wore the cloth. 6, i.e., a man. Because in the first they both agreed that the taking was with permission, and the confessor claims a cause of guarantee, which is the loan, and the other denies it, so the statement is of the other. Contrary to the second. And if the second is like he said: 'You gave me a trust' and the other claimed usurpation, he is not liable. The difference: that in the first he confessed to a cause of guarantee and claimed what exonerates him, and the opponent denied, so the statement is of the opponent. In the second, he claimed, which is the usurpation, and the confessor denies, so the statement is of the confessor. If it is said: his giving it is by his taking possession, so he is confessing to it; it may be by vacating and placing before his hands. And if that necessitates it, then the necessitator has no generality because it is established by necessity, so it is estimated by its measure, so it does not appear in its conclusion as a cause of guarantee. If the confessor refrains from the oath, the thousand becomes binding on him. ('Ayni, Fath, 'Inaya) He took it, i.e., Amr, if it is existing, otherwise its value. ('Ayni) i.e., if Zayd confessed to Amr: 'This thing was a trust with me when I took it from you,' and Amr said: 'Not so, rather this thing is mine,' Amr takes it. Because the taker confessor confessed to the hand for Amr, then to taking from him, which is a cause of guarantee, then claimed entitlement to it, so his claim is not accepted. So the return of the object is obligatory upon him if it is existing, and if not existing, he must return its value. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 225/2) (Fath) It became obligatory on me. So he returned it, i.e., so-and-so returned the camel or the cloth to me, and so-and-so said: 'You lied, rather the cloth and the camel are mine.' ('Ayni) So the statement is of the confessor: i.e., if a man said: 'I hired my camel or this cloth of mine to so-and-so, so so-and-so rode the camel or wore the cloth, then he returned it to me,' and so-and-so said: 'You lied, rather the cloth and the animal are mine, and I took them wrongfully,' so the statement is of the confessor and the other has the evidence. And if he said: 'I received from him a thousand that was for me with him, and he denied,' then he may take it; because he confessed to ownership for him and that he took it by his right and claimed what exonerates him, and the other denies. And this is according to Abu Hanifa as istihsan. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the statement is of the one who took the cloth or the animal, and that is the analogy (qiyas), and the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad?) held it. And on this difference is the case of 'ariyah and iskan: as if he said: 'I lent so-and-so my cloth then I took it from him,' or 'I housed so-and-so in my house then I took it from him,' and so-and-so said: 'It is mine.' The face of qiyas: that he confessed to the hand for him, then claimed entitlement against him, so his confession for him is accepted without his claim, so return is obligatory. The face of istihsan: that the hand in ijarah is established by necessity for the fulfillment of the contracted purpose, which is the usufruct, so it is non-existent beyond the necessity, so it is not a confessor to the hand as a purpose, so it does not appear in the right of entitlement against the confessor. And in 'al-Israr': the difference is when the animal is not known to the confessor; otherwise, his statement is accepted by consensus; because the ownership is known to the confessor. And this is based on what the early scholars held that the judge may judge by his knowledge, although the mufta bihi is what the later scholars mentioned that he does not have that. And if he said: 'So-and-so planted this land, or built this house, or planted this vine, and all that is in the hand of the confessor,' and the confessor said: 'The ownership is mine, and I did that for myself,' and the confessor said: 'No, rather I sought your help and you did it, or you did it for hire,' then the statement is of the confessor.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Confession (Kitab al-Iqrar) discusses scenarios where a person confesses to taking an object from another and the other disputes ownership. The passage type is a series of rulings with rational proofs. The author first presents a case: if someone says 'This was a trust (wadi'a) with me when I took it from you' and the other says 'It is mine,' the taker must return the object. The reason is that the confessor admitted to having the object in his hand and then taking it, which establishes a cause for liability (daman). If the object is still in existence, it must be returned; if it has perished, its value must be paid. Then a distinction is made between two scenarios: in the first (trust), both parties agree that the taking was with permission, and the confessor claims a cause of liability (i.e., he took it as a loan or rent) while the other denies, so the other's statement (denying liability) is accepted. In the second (when the confessor says 'You gave me a trust' and the other claims usurpation), the confessor denies the liability cause, so his statement is accepted. The text then moves to a case of ijarah: a man says 'I rented my camel or cloth to so-and-so, he rode it/wore it, and returned it,' and the other says 'You lied, it is mine.' Here, according to Abu Hanifa (istihsan), the statement of the lessor (confessor) is accepted. But Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold qiyas: the statement of the taker is accepted because he admitted the hand of the lessor. The difference hinges on the nature of the hand in ijarah: it is established by necessity for usufruct, so it does not imply ownership. The later case: if the confessor says that another person planted, built, or planted on property in his hand, and the other claims ownership, the confessor's statement is accepted because he is merely alleging an act, not confessing to a hand or ownership. This lesson covers the first part of the text up to the ijarah case. The Hanafi position is clear: the muqir (confessor) is believed when he claims the item is his due to a valid cause, unless the other has evidence.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission of a right against oneself.
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference based on equity or necessity, overriding qiyas.
يد (yad): Hand; legal possession or control over an object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the ijarah dispute, which Hanafi imam's view is the mufta bihi?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) All three agree

Key Takeaway
A confessor who admits to taking an object with permission must return it unless he can prove a cause of liability; in ijarah, the lessor's statement is accepted due to the functional nature of the lessee's hand.

Definition of Marad al-Mawt and the One-Third Rule
Definition of marad al-mawt and limitation of tabarru'at to one-third

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of marad al-mawt and apply the rule that tabarru'at are limited to one-third of the estate.

Core Idea
A terminally ill person's gifts are valid only up to one-third, based on the definition that his predominant state is death.

This passage defines who counts as a 'sick person' (marīḍ al-mawt) for legal purposes, specifically for the limitation on gratuitous acts. Understanding this definition is crucial because it determines the validity of gifts and acknowledgements made during terminal illness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The chapter is on the sick person's acknowledgement (iqrar) and is placed at the end because illness is an exceptional state, and rulings differ from the healthy.
The healthy person's acts are unrestricted; the sick are limited to one-third.
2
List the Proposed Definitions
The passage records several definitions from Hanafi authorities: unable to stand without help, bedridden even if can stand, unable to walk without support, unable to pray standing, and finally 'one whose predominant state is death'.
These definitions show the evolution towards the mufta bihi view.
3
Identify the Mufta Bihi Definition
The text concludes with 'this is the sick person whose gifts are valid from one-third', referring to the definition: 'one whose predominant state is death' (من كان غالب حاله الموت).
This is the operative definition for the one-third limitation.
4
Derive the Ruling for Tabarru'at
For a person meeting this definition, all gratuitous acts (gifts, acknowledgements without known cause) are valid up to one-third of the estate; any excess is suspended on the consent of the heirs.
If heirs do not consent, the excess is batil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب إقرار المريض [يعني به من هو في مرض الموت. (فتح) أخره إما لأن المرض عارض والأصل عدمه، أو لأن في إقرار المريض اختلافاً في بعض الصور، بخلاف إقرار الصحيح، فكان أقوى، وأفرده بباب على حدة؛ لاختصاصه بأحكام ليست للصحيح، واختلفوا في حد المريض، فقال بعضهم: هو من لا يقدر أن يقوم بنفسه إلا أن يقيمه الإنسان وقيل هو صاحب الفراش وإن كان يقوم بنفسه، وقيل: هو من لا يقدر على المشي إلا أن يتهادى بين اثنين وقال الفقيه أبو الليث: هو من لا يقدر على أن يصلي قائماً، وقيل: هو من كان غالب حاله الموت، فهذا هو المريض الذي تكون تبرعاته جائزة من الثلث. (عيني، فتح، جوهري)
Chapter of the Sick Person's Acknowledgement: Meaning one who is in the illness of death. (Fath) It was placed at the end either because illness is an accidental state and the default is its absence, or because the acknowledgement of the sick person differs in some cases from the acknowledgement of the healthy person [which is stronger, so it was placed separately; due to its specialization with rulings not for the healthy. And they differed in the definition of the sick person: Some said: He is the one who cannot stand on his own except if someone helps him to stand. And it was said: He is the one who keeps to the bed even if he can stand on his own. And it was said: He is the one who cannot walk except while leaning on two men. And Abu al-Layth said: He is the one who cannot pray standing. And it was said: He is the one whose predominant state is death. This is the sick person whose gifts are valid from one-third. (Ayni, Fath, Jawhari)
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage defines the legally relevant 'sick person' for the chapter on acknowledgements. The text first explains why this chapter is placed at the end of the book: illness is an exceptional state, and the rulings for the sick person have unique features not found for the healthy. Then it records multiple definitions of the sick person from Hanafi authorities. The final definition - one whose predominant state is death - is the operative one for the rule that gratuitous acts (tabarru'at) are valid only from one-third of his wealth. This is a crucial distinction between the healthy and the terminally ill: the healthy person may dispose of all his wealth, while the sick person's generosity is limited to one-third to protect the rights of his heirs and creditors.

Key Terms
مريض الموت (marīḍ al-mawt): A person whose illness is likely to lead to death, regardless of ability to walk or stand.
تبرعات (tabarru'āt): Voluntary gifts or dispositions without exchange, including acknowledgements that are gratuitous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One who cannot stand without help
B) One who keeps to the bed
C) One whose predominant state is death
D) One who cannot pray standing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of marad al-mawt is one whose predominant state is death; their tabarru'at are valid only up to one-third of their estate, protecting heirs' and creditors' rights.

Priority of Debts Over Acknowledged Debts in Terminal Illness
States priority rule and inter-madhhab argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prioritizes health debts and known-cause debts over acknowledged debts during terminal illness and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Health debts attach to property in terminal illness because the sick cannot earn; later acknowledgments cannot compete.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical dispute: when a terminally ill debtor has both prior health debts and later acknowledgments of new debts, which are paid first? The Hanafi ruling prioritizes health debts and known-cause debts, citing the debtor's inability to earn in illness. The Shafi'i school disagrees, holding all debts equal. We will explore the proofs and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Health debts (dīn al-ṣiḥḥa) and debts incurred during illness by a known cause (e.g., witnessed loan, purchase) are given precedence over debts merely acknowledged during illness.
The acknowledged debt is still valid but subordinate.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Malik and Ahmad) hold that all debts—health, illness by known cause, and acknowledged—are equal and should be paid proportionally.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument: acknowledgement is a rational act free from suspicion; the dhimmah can bear multiple rights, so no priority is needed.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
During health, the debtor can earn and pay all debts, so creditors' rights do not attach to specific property. During terminal illness, the debtor cannot earn, and thus creditors' rights attach to the existing property to prevent loss. The sick person is interdicted (maḥjūr) from acknowledging debts to the detriment of prior creditors.
This is a classic application of istihsan based on the difference in capacity.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In the Hanafi school, health creditors are paid in full first before any acknowledged debts. In the Shafi'i school, all creditors share the estate proportionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دين الصحة وما لزمه في مرضه بسبب معروف قدم على ما أقر به في مرضه، وأخر مطلقا أي الدين الذي الإرث عنه، وإن أقر . أي مرض موته بسبب معروف: وهو كل دين وجب عليه من ثمن مال ملكه أو استهلكه أو علم وجوبه بالبينة. (عيني) قدم على إلخ : أي إذا أقر الرجل في مرض موته بديون، وعليه ديون في صحة وديون لزمته في مرضه بأسباب معلومة من القرض والشراء والتزوج بمهر المثل، وعاين الشهود هذه الأسباب فدين الصحة والديون المعروفة الأسباب مقدم على ما أقر به في مرضه ولو وديعة؛ لأن المريض محجور عن الإقرار بالدين ما لم يفرغ عن دين الصحة، فالدين الثابت بإقرار المحجور لا يزاحم الدين الثابت بلا حجر، وليس له أن يقضي دين بعض الغرماء دون بعض. والمراد بالسبب المعروف البينة أو معاينة قاض، وهو ما ليس بتبرع؛ فإن تبرعه جائز من ومقدم على الديون. الثلث وأخر الإرث عنه: أي عن الدين الذي أقر به في حالة المرض؛ لأن الورثة لا تستحق شيئاً من مال الميت ما دام عليه دين فهذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي به دين المرض ودين الصحة يستويان؛ لأنه إقرار لا تهمة فيه؛ إذ هو صادر عن عقل، والذمة قابلة للحقوق في الحالين وبه قال مالك وأحمد ولنا أن حق غرماء الصحة تعلق بمال المريض مرض الموت في أول مرضه؛ لأنه عجز عن قضائه من مال آخر بعجزه عن الاكتساب، والإقرار به صادف حق غرماء الصحة، فكان محجوراً . عنه، وإنما استوى الدين المعروف السبب ودين الصحة؛ لأنه لما علم سببه انتفت التهمة في الإقرار به رمز الحقائق: ٢٢٦/٢] فإن قيل: لو تعلق حق الغرماء بمال المديون بطل إقراره بالدين حال الصحة؛ لأن الإقرار المتضمن لإبطال حق الغرماء غير معتبر ، أجيب بأنه في حال الصحة لم يتعلق بالمال؛ لقدرته على الاكتساب و لم يحتج إلى تعليق حق الغرماء بماله، وحالة المرض حالة عجز عن الاكتساب، فيتعلق حقهم به حذراً عن التوى. (فتح، عناية)
The debt of health and what became due in his illness by a known cause are given precedence over what he acknowledged in his illness, and inheritance is absolutely deferred from the debt acknowledged in his illness. 'By a known cause': every debt that became due for price of goods he owned or consumed, or whose obligation was known by evidence. (Ayni) 'Given precedence': If a man acknowledges debts in his terminal illness, and he has health debts and debts that became due in his illness by known causes such as loan, purchase, and marriage with equal dower, and the witnesses witnessed these causes, then the health debt and the debts of known causes are given precedence over what he acknowledged in his illness, even if it is a deposit; because the sick person is interdicted from acknowledging a debt until he satisfies the health debt. So the debt established by an interdicted person's acknowledgement does not compete with a debt established without interdiction, and he is not allowed to pay some creditors over others. The meaning of 'known cause' is evidence or a judge's witnessing, and it is what is not a gift; for his gift is valid from one-third and given precedence over debts. 'And inheritance is deferred': i.e., from the debt acknowledged in the state of illness; because the heirs do not deserve anything from the deceased's estate as long as there is a debt upon him. This is our position. Al-Shafi'i said: The illness debt and the health debt are equal; because it is an acknowledgement in which there is no suspicion; since it issues from a rational mind, and the dhimmah is capable of bearing rights in both states. Malik and Ahmad said the same. Our proof: The right of the health creditors attaches to the property of the sick person in terminal illness from the start of his illness; because he is unable to pay it from other property due to his inability to earn, and the acknowledgement meets the right of the health creditors, so he is interdicted from it. The debt of known cause and health debt are equal because when its cause is known, suspicion in acknowledging it is removed. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/226) If it is said: If the creditors' right attached to the debtor's property, his acknowledgement of debt during health would be invalid; because an acknowledgement that entails nullifying the creditors' right is not considered. The answer: During health, the right did not attach to the property; because he had the ability to earn and did not need to attach the creditors' right to his property. The state of illness is a state of inability to earn, so their right attaches to it to avoid loss. (Fath, Inayah)
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage explains the priority of debts over acknowledgements during terminal illness. The key principle: debts that are established during health (dīn al-ṣiḥḥa) or during illness by a known cause (e.g., loan, purchase of a specific item witnessed) take precedence over debts merely acknowledged without a known cause. The reason is that the sick person is legally interdicted (maḥjūr) from acknowledging debts to the detriment of existing creditors. The passage also addresses the Shafi'i counter-argument that there should be no priority since acknowledgement is a rational act. The Hanafi response distinguishes between health and illness: during health, the debtor can earn and pay all debts, so creditor rights do not attach to specific property; during terminal illness, the debtor cannot earn, so creditor rights attach to the existing property to prevent loss. This is a classic example of istihsan based on the difference in capacity.

Key Terms
دين الصحة (dīn al-ṣiḥḥa): A debt incurred while the debtor was healthy.
سبب معروف (sabab maʿrūf): A known cause such as a witnessed loan or purchase; something that is not a pure gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why are health debts prioritized over debts acknowledged during terminal illness?
A) Because the patient is insane.
B) Because the health creditor's right attaches to property due to the debtor's inability to earn in illness.
C) Because acknowledgements during illness are invalid.
D) Because all debts are equal.

Key Takeaway
Health debts and known-cause illness debts take priority over mere acknowledgments in terminal illness because the sick person is interdicted from harming prior creditors due to inability to earn.

Acknowledgement to an Heir vs. Stranger in Terminal Illness
Ruling with proof: Acknowledgement in terminal illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on acknowledgement by a terminally ill person to an heir versus a stranger, and apply the condition of heir consent to determine validity.

Core Idea
Acknowledgement to an heir is invalid unless all other heirs consent; to a stranger it is valid even if it takes all the wealth.

The Hanafi school treats a terminally ill person's acknowledgement (iqrār) like a bequest (waṣiyyah): it cannot benefit an heir without the consent of other heirs. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from hadith, the rationale of protecting heir rights, and the contrasting views of other schools. Understanding this distinction is vital for advising clients in estate planning and dispute resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes acknowledgement to an heir from acknowledgement to a stranger. Note that each has a different ruling: invalid vs. valid.
The key factor is whether the beneficiary is a potential heir at the time of acknowledgement.
2
Locate the primary proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'لا وصية لوارث ولا إقرار له بالدين' (No bequest to an heir nor acknowledgement of a debt for him). Recognize that this hadith, though ahad, is considered qat'i al-dalala in prohibiting such acknowledgements.
The proof is naqli (textual) and is not overridden by istihsan here.
3
Examine the role of other heirs' consent
The conditional 'إلا أن يصدقه البقية' (unless the rest confirm him) shows that the prohibition is not absolute—it is for the protection of other heirs. Their consent lifts the interdiction.
Compare with bequest exceeding one-third: that requires consent only after death, while here consent can be given during life.
4
Compare with other schools
The passage contrasts Shafi'i (valid because owner of wealth), Maliki (valid if no suspicion), and Hanbali (limited to one-third). Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) in each.
The Hanafi reliance on the hadith and harm principle is distinctive.
5
Apply the rule to subsidiary cases
Consider related scenarios: acknowledgement of paternity after acknowledging to a stranger, acknowledgement to a woman then marrying her, and acknowledgement of receiving a debt from an heir. Each follows the same principle.
These furu' illustrate the consistency of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المريض لوارثه بطل إلا أن يصدقه البقية، وإن أقر لأجنبي صح وإن أحاط بماله، بدين أو عين أي الإقرار من الورثة المريض بدين أو عين الإقرار لعدم التهمة إقراره أي استغرق وإن أقر لأجنبي ثم أقر ببنوته، ثبت نسبه وبطل إقراره، وإن أقر لأجنبية ثم نكحها المريض بدين أو عين لاله أي بأنه ابن له صح، بخلاف الهبة والوصية أي إقرارها لامرأة أجنبية أي تزوجها كما يصح في بطل: أي الإقرار، وقال الشافعي: لا يبطل ؛ لأنه مالك للمال - كما لو أقر به لغيره – فيصح حال الصحة، وعند مالك: يصح إذا لم يتهم، ولنا: قوله عليه: 'لا وصية لوارث ولا إقرار له بالدين'، ولأنه ضرر لبقية الورثة. إلا أن يصدقه البقية: لأن الحجر كان لحقهم، فإذا صدقوه فقد أقروا بتقدمه عليهم فيلزمهم، وكذا لو كان له دين على وارثه فأقر بقبضه لا يصح إلا أن يصدقه البقية رمز الحقائق: ٢٢٦/٢] فإذا صدقوه في حياة المقر فلا حاجة إلى التصديق بعد الموت، بخلاف الوصية بما زاد على الثلث حيث لا ينفذ إلا بإجازة الورثة بعد موت الموصي، ولو ادعى المقر له أن الإقرار في الصحة وكذبه بقية الورثة فالقول لهم، ولو أقاما البينة فبينة المقر له أولى. (فتح) وإن أقر لأجنبي إلخ: يعني وإن أقر بجميع ماله وليس عليه دين ولو في المرض بسبب معروف، وعند أحمد: يصح إقراره إلا في الثلث وهو القياس؛ لأن الشرع قصر تصرفه على الثلث ولنا أثر ابن عمر ، فإنه قال: إذا أقر الرجل في مرضه لرجل غير وارث، فإنه جائز وإن أحاط بماله، ولأنه لو لم يقبل إقراره، لامتنع الناس عن معاملته حذراً من إتواء مالهم فينسد عليهم طريق التجارة أو المداينة. (عيني، فتح، زيلعي)
The sick person's [acknowledgement] to his heir is invalid unless the rest of the heirs confirm it. And if he acknowledges to a stranger, it is valid even if it encompasses all his wealth, whether for a debt or an article. 'From the heirs': the sick person's acknowledgement of a debt or an article [is valid] due to lack of suspicion. '...': 'his acknowledgement' i.e., it encompasses. And if he acknowledges to a stranger and then acknowledges his paternity, his lineage is established and his [first] acknowledgement is invalidated. And if he acknowledges to a woman stranger and then marries her, the sick person's acknowledgement of a debt or article is valid, unlike the gift and bequest. '...': the acknowledgement to a woman stranger, i.e., he marries her, as is valid in ... invalid: i.e., the acknowledgement. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not invalidated; because he is the owner of the wealth—as if he acknowledged to someone else—so it is valid in health. According to Malik: It is valid if there is no suspicion. Our proof: His statement (peace be upon him): 'No bequest for an heir nor acknowledgement of a debt for him,' and because it harms the rest of the heirs. 'Unless the rest confirm him': because the interdiction was for their right; so if they confirm, they have acknowledged its precedence over them, so it is binding upon them. Similarly, if he had a debt upon his heir and he acknowledged receiving it, it is not valid unless the rest confirm. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/226) If they confirm during the lifetime of the acknowledger, there is no need for confirmation after death, unlike the bequest exceeding one-third which is not executed without the heirs' permission after the testator's death. If the acknowledgedee claims that the acknowledgement was in health and the rest of the heirs deny him, the statement is theirs; but if both produce evidence, the evidence of the acknowledgedee is preferred. (Fath) 'And if he acknowledges to a stranger etc.': meaning if he acknowledges all his wealth and he has no debt, even during illness due to a known cause, according to Ahmad it is valid except for one-third, which is the analogy because the law restricted his disposition to one-third. Our proof: the athar of Ibn Umar: he said: 'When a man acknowledges during his illness to a non-heir, it is valid even if it encompasses all his wealth,' and because if his acknowledgement were not accepted, people would refrain from dealing with him for fear of losing their wealth, thus closing the path of trade or debt. (Ayni, Fath, Zayla'i)
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage covers two interconnected rulings. First, an acknowledgement by a terminally ill person to one of his heirs is invalid—it is treated like a bequest to an heir, which is prohibited by hadith. However, if all other heirs consent, it becomes valid. Second, an acknowledgement to a stranger (non-heir) is fully valid even if it consumes the entire estate. This is supported by an athar from Ibn Umar and by practical necessity: if such acknowledgements were restricted to one-third, people would avoid dealing with the sick. The passage also addresses the Shafi'i view that acknowledging to an heir might be valid, countering with the hadith 'لا وصية لوارث ولا إقرار له بالدين'. The ruling is a clear example of how the Hanafi school balances creditor rights, heir rights, and practical transaction needs.

Key Terms
وارث (wārith): A person who would inherit from the patient if he died at the time of acknowledgement.
إقرار (iqrār): An admission of a right (debt or property) that was due prior to the acknowledgement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is an acknowledgement to a stranger by a terminally ill person valid even if it consumes the entire estate?
A) Because the stranger is not an heir and thus no harm is done.
B) Because the patient is not likely to be lying to a stranger.
C) Because the Prophet said 'No bequest for an heir', implying permission for strangers.
D) Because of the athar of Ibn Umar and practical necessity to keep trade open.

Key Takeaway
A terminally ill person's acknowledgement to an heir is invalid unless all other heirs consent, while acknowledgement to a stranger is fully valid—this protects heir rights while enabling normal transactions.

Subsequent Paternity vs Marriage: Effect on Prior Acknowledgment
Ruling distinguishing effects of subsequent paternity and marriage on prior acknowledgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of subsequent paternity and subsequent marriage on a prior acknowledgment, and explain the legal rationale based on retroactivity of lineage vs prospective nature of marriage.

Core Idea
Paternity retroacts, marriage does not: a subsequent paternity invalidates a prior acknowledgment; a subsequent marriage does not.

Acknowledgment (iqrār) is a binding declaration. But what happens if, after acknowledging a debt to a stranger, the debtor later discovers that person is his child, or marries the creditor? The Hanafi school draws a sharp line: paternity invalidates the prior acknowledgment because it retroactively shows the person was an heir; marriage does not because it only creates heirship prospectively. This lesson unpacks that distinction and contrasts it with gifts and bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: (1) a sick person acknowledges to a stranger and later acknowledges paternity of that person; (2) a sick person acknowledges to a stranger and later marries that person. Determine the ruling in each.
2
Analyze the paternity case: retroactivity of lineage
Lineage traces back to the time of conception (waqt al-‘ulūq). Therefore, if paternity is established, the person was actually an heir at the moment of the first acknowledgment. Since acknowledgment to an heir is invalid, the first acknowledgment is void.
Condition: the acknowledgedee must confirm the paternity (taṣdīq al-muqarr lahu).
3
Analyze the marriage case: prospectiveness of marriage
Marriage does not retroactively create heirship; it only makes the spouse an heir upon death. Hence, the prior acknowledgment remains valid because at the time it was made, there was no suspicion (tuhma).
Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing marriage creates suspicion; the majority Hanafi response is that marriage is prospective.
4
Compare with gifts and bequests
If a sick person gives a gift or makes a bequest to a stranger and then marries that person, the gift/bequest is invalidated by consensus. Reason: bequests take effect after death (when the spouse is an heir), and gifts during illness are treated like bequests.
This contrast highlights that the ruling on acknowledgment is specific and does not extend to gratuitous transfers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أقر لأجنبي ثم أقر ببنوته، ثبت نسبه وبطل إقراره، وإن أقر لأجنبية ثم نكحها صح، بخلاف الهبة والوصية ثبوت نسبه: أي لو أقر المريض لأجنبي مجهول النسب، ثم أقر بأنه ابن له ثبت نسبه؛ لأن الإقرار بالنسب من الحوائج الأصلية؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى بقاء نسله، وحاجته مقدمة على حق الورثة، ولا تهمة فيه، ولكنه يشترط في ثبوت نسبه، ووجود التصديق من المقر له حيث كان من أهل التصديق بأن كان يعبر عن نفسه. لا وبطل إقراره لأنه تبين أنه أقر للوارث (عيني)] لأن دعوى النسب تستند إلى وقت العلوق، فيظهر أن البنوة ثابتة وقت الإقرار ولو لم يثبت نسبه بأن كذبه المقر له، أو عرف نسبه صح الإقرار؛ لعدم ثبوت النسب، وعندمالك: لا يبطل إقراره في صورة ثبوت النسب إذا لم يتهم (عيني، فتح صح: أي إقراره لأجنبية نكحها بعد الإقرار، وقال زفر: لا يصح؛ لحصول التهمة؛ لأنها وارثة عند الموت ولنا أنه أقر وليس بينهما سبب التهمة، فلايبطل الإقرار بسبب يحدث بعده [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٢٦/٢] لأن الزوجية تقتصر على زمان التزوج، بخلاف النسب، فإنه يستند إلى وقت العلوق . (فتح) بخلاف الهبة والوصية أي لو وهب المريض أو أوصى لأجنبية ثم تزوجها تبطل الهبة والوصية اتفاقاً؛ لأن الوصية تمليك بعد الموت، وهي وارثة حينئذ فلا يصح، والهبة في المرض وصية حتى لا تنفذ إلا من الثلث، فلا تصح للوارث كما لا تصح الوصية. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٢٦/٢]
And if he acknowledges to a stranger and then acknowledges his paternity, his lineage is established and his [first] acknowledgement is invalidated. And if he acknowledges to a woman stranger and then marries her, it is valid, unlike the gift and bequest. 'Establishment of lineage': If the sick person acknowledges to a stranger of unknown lineage, then acknowledges that he is his son, his lineage is established; because acknowledgement of lineage is among the original needs; since he needs to preserve his progeny, and his need is given precedence over the right of the heirs, and there is no suspicion in it. But it is required for the establishment of his lineage the presence of confirmation from the acknowledgedee if he is capable of confirmation, i.e., he can express himself. No, and his acknowledgement is invalidated because it becomes clear that he acknowledged to an heir (Ayni). Because the claim of lineage traces back to the time of impregnation, so it appears that the sonship was established at the time of acknowledgement. And if his lineage is not established—for example, if the acknowledgedee denies him, or his lineage is known—the acknowledgement remains valid; due to non-establishment of lineage. According to Malik: His acknowledgement is not invalidated in the case of established lineage if there is no suspicion. (Ayni, Fath) 'Valid': i.e., his acknowledgement to a woman stranger whom he marries after the acknowledgement. Zufar said: It is not valid; due to the occurrence of suspicion, because she is an heir at death. Our proof: He acknowledged when there was no cause for suspicion between them, so the acknowledgement is not invalidated by something that occurs after it. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/226) Because marriage is limited to the time of marriage, unlike lineage, which traces back to the time of impregnation. (Fath) 'Unlike the gift and bequest': If the sick person gives a gift or bequest to a woman stranger and then marries her, the gift and bequest are invalidated by consensus; because the bequest is a transfer after death, and she is an heir then, so it is not valid; and the gift during illness is [like] a bequest, so it is not executed except from one-third, so it is not valid for an heir just as a bequest is not valid. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/226)
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two types of subsequent events affecting a prior acknowledgement. (1) If the patient acknowledges a debt to a stranger and later acknowledges that the same person is his son, the paternity is established (subject to the acknowledgedee's confirmation) and the prior acknowledgement is invalidated. The reason: paternity relates back to the time of conception (waqt al-‘ulūq), so the person was actually an heir at the time of the first acknowledgement. Since acknowledgement to an heir is invalid, the first acknowledgement becomes void. (2) If the patient acknowledges a debt to a woman and later marries her, the acknowledgement remains valid. Zufar argued that marriage creates suspicion because she becomes an heir, but the majority Hanafi response is that marriage only creates inheritance upon death and does not retroactively affect the earlier acknowledgement. The rationale: marriage is prospective (muqtaṣirah ‘alā zamān al-tazawwuj), while lineage is retroactive. The passage also contrasts this with gifts and bequests: if the patient gives a gift or makes a will to a woman and then marries her, both are invalidated by consensus because bequests are effective after death (when she is an heir) and gifts during illness are treated like bequests.

Key Terms
علوق (‘ulūq): The time of conception from which lineage is traced back.
تصديق المقر له (taṣdīq al-muqarr lahu): The confirmation by the person in whose favor the acknowledgement is made; required for paternity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a subsequent acknowledgement of paternity invalidate a prior acknowledgement to that person, but a subsequent marriage does not?
A) Because lineage is more important than debt
B) Because paternity relates back to conception, making the person an heir at the time of first acknowledgement; marriage only creates heirship at death
C) Because marriage creates stronger suspicion
D) Because the hadeeth only mentions paternity

Key Takeaway
Paternity retroacts to conception, marriage does not; thus only paternity (or its equivalent) invalidates prior acknowledgment.
