Oath of the Denying Heir in Acknowledgment of Debt
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions in the intra-Hanafi dispute about the oath for the denying heir and apply the preferred view (mufta bihi) to a new scenario.

Core Idea
The oath of the denying heir protects the acknowledging brother's share, not the debtor's right.

This passage explores a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school. The base ruling is straightforward: one heir's acknowledgment of partial debt collection is binding only on his own share. But the question arises: must the other heir swear an oath? Different authorities weigh the purpose of the oath differently. We will dissect the arguments and see how the later school settled the matter.

Guided Path
1
Understand the base case
Two sons inherit a debt of 100 dirhams from their father. One son acknowledges that the father collected 50 dirhams from the debtor. What is the immediate ruling?
The acknowledging son's admission is valid only against his own share; he gets nothing from the 50, and the other son (denying) gets the entire 50 from the debtor.
2
Grasp the legal effect and the circularity argument
The acknowledging heir cannot recourse against his brother for half of the collected amount, even if they both agree on joint ownership. Why? Because it would lead to circular litigation: brother sues debtor, debtor sues acknowledging heir.
This establishes the finality of the acknowledgment: it binds only the acknowledging heir's share.
3
Identify the dispute about the oath
Should the denying heir be required to swear an oath that he has no knowledge of the collection? Two views: (1) No oath when the acknowledgment is for a part equal to the acknowledging heir's share (al-Bahr, al-Zayla'i); (2) Oath required in both partial and full acknowledgment cases (Mulla Miskin, al-Durar).
The dispute hinges on the purpose of the oath: is it to protect the debtor or the acknowledging brother?
4
Analyze the tarjih and the author's preference
The author (Habib al-Rahman) sides with the oath-required view, citing al-Durar. He argues that al-Zayla'i's no-oath position only considers the debtor's right, but the oath here is for the acknowledging brother's right to claim a share if the denying heir fails to swear.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that the denying heir is sworn in both cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ترك ابنين وله على آخر مائة فأقر أحدهما بقبض أبيه خمسين منها، فلا شيء للميت للمقر، وللآخر خمسون. أي درهما أي مائة درهم أي أحد الابنين أي من المائة فلا شيء للمقر : ولا يرجع المقر على أخيه بنصف ما قبض، وإن تصادقا على الاشتراك في المقبوض؛ لأنه لو رجع على أخيه لرجع أخوه على الغريم، فيرجع الغريم على المقر بقدر ذلك، لا لانتقاض المقاصة في ذلك القدر، وبقائه دينا على الميت والدين مقدم على الإرث، فيؤدي إلى الدور. (فتح) وللآخر خمسون: أي وللابن الآخر الذي لم يقر بقبض أبيه خمسين خمسون درهماً، وهل يحلف المنكر أم لا؟ ففي البحر": أن لا يحلف في هذه الصورة، حيث قال: وإقرار أحد الورثة باستيفاء الميت دينه أي كله صحيح في حصته فقط، ويحلف المنكر على نفي العلم، بخلاف إقراره باستيفاء البعض قدر ميراثه فإنه لا يحلف المنكر، والله أعلم. وحاصله : أنه إذا أقر بعض الورثة بأن الميت استوفى جميع دينه صح إقراره في حصته، ويحلف المنكر، وإذا أقر باستيفاء بعض دينه بقدر حصة المقر ، كما هو مسألة المتن لا يحلف المنكر، وقال في "ملا مسكين": يحلف في مسألة المتن أيضاً، حيث قال: وللآخر خمسون بعد ما يحلف بالله ما تعلم أن أباك قبض منه مائة، انتهى، قال في "الفتح": تعقبه الشيخ شاهين بأن مسألة المتن لا تحليف فيها، ولعله سبق قلم وإنما التحليف فيما إذا أقر أن أباه قبض كل الدين فإن نكل أي المنكر برئت ذمته أي المديون وإن حلف دفع إليه نصيبه، بخلاف المسألة الأولى، حيث لا يحلف؛ لحق الغريم، كما في "الزيلعي"؛ لأن حقه كله حصل له من جهة المقر فلا حاجة إلى تحليفه، وهنا لم يحصل له إلا النصف فيحلفا، انتهى. أقول: قول الزيلعي بخلاف المسألة الأولى، حيث لا يحلف حق الغريم لا ينافي ما ذكره الشارح من أنه يحلف؛ لأن تحليفه لا لحق الغريم بل لحق أخيه المقر؛ إذ لو نكل عن الحلف شاركه المقر في نصف المائة، ولهذا صرح في "الدرر" بأنه يحلف في كل من المسألتين، فقول الشيخ شاهين: مسألة المتن لا تحليف فيها ولعله سبق قلم غير مسلم، انتهى ما في "الفتح" بتصرف. (حبيب الرحمن الديوبندي)
And if he leaves two sons and has a hundred (dirhams) against another person, and one of them acknowledges that his father received fifty of it then nothing of the deceased goes to the acknowledging (son) – meaning one of the two sons – meaning from the hundred – so nothing goes to the acknowledging (son): and the acknowledging (son) does not recourse against his brother for half of what was received, even if they both agree on their joint ownership of the received amount; because if he recourses against his brother, his brother would recourse against the debtor, and the debtor would recourse against the acknowledging (son) to that extent, not because the set-off is broken in that amount, but because it remains a debt against the deceased and the debt has priority over inheritance, thus leading to circularity. (Fath) And for the other fifty: meaning for the other son who did not acknowledge his father received fifty – fifty dirhams. And is the denying (son) to be sworn or not? In al-Bahr: that he is not sworn in this case, where he said: The acknowledgment of one of the heirs that the deceased collected his debt entirely is valid only with respect to his share, and the denying (heir) is sworn (to deny knowledge), contrary to his acknowledgment of collection of part (of the debt) to the extent of the acknowledging heir's share – as in the text's case – then the denying heir is not sworn. And Allah knows best. Its summary: When one of the heirs acknowledges that the deceased collected all his debt, his acknowledgment is valid in his share, and the denying (heir) is sworn; and if he acknowledges the collection of some of the debt to the extent of the acknowledging heir's share – as in the text's case – the denying (heir) is not sworn. And in "Mulla Miskin": he is sworn in the text's case too, where he said: "And for the other fifty after he swears by Allah, 'I do not know that your father collected a hundred from him'" end quote. In al-Fath: Sheikh Shahin criticized this, saying the text's case has no swearing, and perhaps it was a slip of the pen. Swearing is only when he acknowledges that his father collected the entire debt; if the denying (heir) fails to swear, the debtor's liability is discharged; and if he swears, his share is paid to him, contrary to the first case where he is not sworn due to the right of the debtor, as in al-Zayla'i, because his entire right came to him from the acknowledging (heir), so there is no need to swear him; but here he received only half, so they both swear. End. I say: al-Zayla'i's statement about the first case, where he is not sworn due to the right of the debtor, does not contradict what the commentator said about him being sworn, because his swearing is not for the debtor's right but for the right of his acknowledging brother; because if he fails to swear, the acknowledging brother shares half of the hundred with him. For this reason, it is stated in al-Durar that he is sworn in both cases. So Sheikh Shahin's statement that the text's case has no swearing, and perhaps it was a slip of the pen, is not acceptable. End of what is in al-Fath with adaptation. (Habib al-Rahman al-Diyubandi)
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether the denying heir must swear an oath when one heir acknowledges partial collection of a debt owed to the deceased. The base ruling from the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states: if a man leaves two sons and is owed 100 dirhams, and one son acknowledges that the father collected 50 dirhams of that debt, then the acknowledging son gets nothing from the deceased's estate in that 50 dirhams (because his acknowledgment is valid against his own share only), and the other son gets 50 dirhams from the debtor. The commentary first explains why the acknowledging son cannot recourse against his brother: circularity would result. Then it addresses the question of whether the denying son must swear an oath. There are two positions: (1) The view in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Zayla'i: if the acknowledgment is for part of the debt equal to the acknowledging heir's share (as here), the denying heir is not sworn; but if the acknowledgment is for the entire debt, the denying heir is sworn. The reason for not swearing here is that the debtor's right to the full payment already came from the acknowledging heir, so no need. (2) The view of Mulla Miskin and al-Durar: the denying heir is sworn in both cases, because his swearing is for the right of his acknowledging brother (who could claim half if the denying heir fails to swear). Sheikh Shahin objected to swearing in the partial-acknowledgment case, calling it a slip of the pen, but the author (Habib al-Rahman) defends the position of swearing, citing al-Durar and arguing that al-Zayla'i's statement about not swearing only pertains to the debtor's right, not the brother's right. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position appears to be that the denying heir is sworn in both cases, as per al-Durar. This illustrates a nuance in Hanafi procedure: the purpose of the oath determines its necessity.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgement; a confession that a right is due to another. Here, one heir acknowledges that the father collected part of a debt.
منكر (munkir): The denying party; here, the other son who does not acknowledge the partial collection and disputes the claim.
تحليف (tahlif): Administering an oath; the act of making the denying party swear to the truth of his denial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (mufta bihi) in the passage, what happens if the denying heir refuses to swear an oath in the case where one heir acknowledges partial collection equal to his share?
A) The debtor is discharged from the entire debt.
B) The acknowledging heir receives half of the collected amount from the debtor.
C) The denying heir receives nothing.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in this intra-Hanafi dispute is that the denying heir must swear an oath even when the acknowledgment is for part of the debt, because the oath protects the acknowledging brother's right to claim a share if the denying heir cannot swear truthfully.

The Permissibility of Sulh (Compromise) with Denial and Silence
Inter-madhhab dispute on sulh with denial/silence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on sulh (compromise) to cases of acknowledgment, denial, and silence, and evaluate the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
Sulh is permissible with denial and silence — the general hadith permits all compromise except that which changes the lawful/unlawful.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on sulh (compromise) when a defendant denies the claim or remains silent. While all schools agree on sulh with acknowledgment, the Hanafi school extends it to these two other scenarios based on the general permissibility in the hadith. We will also explore the Shafi'i objection that such sulh amounts to bribery and how the Hanafi scholars rebut it.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Recognize that the Hanafi school holds sulh valid in three scenarios: when the defendant admits (iqrar), denies (inkar), or remains silent (sukut).
This is based on the generality of the hadith 'Every sulh is permissible...'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i restricts sulh to acknowledgment only, arguing that sulh with denial or silence is like bribery (rishwa) because the plaintiff takes property without right from the defendant's perspective.
The Shafi'i view is that such sulh makes the unlawful lawful.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument: Since the defendant denies any liability, any payment made is not a right; hence the plaintiff's receipt is unlawful. Therefore the contract is a compromise that changes the lawful into unlawful.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the hadith's exception ('makes the unlawful lawful') applies only to specific matters (e.g., using pork or wine as consideration). Moreover, from the plaintiff's viewpoint, he receives his claimed right or its substitute; from the defendant's, he pays to avoid an oath and litigation. Thus the sulh is valid.
The exception does not cover the general case of denial/silence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi: sulh with denial/silence is valid and binding, plaintiff acquires ownership of the settlement object. Shafi'i: such sulh is invalid and the plaintiff does not own what he receives.
This affects the enforceability of the settlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تعريف الصلح وأنواعه
كتاب الصلح
هو عقد يرفع النزاع وهو جائز بإقرار وسكوت
أي الصلح في الشرع
أي الصلح أي بإقرار المدعى عليه

كتاب الصلح: اسم من المصالحة، وهو خلاف المخاصمة. ملا مسكين] مناسبة سابقه أن الصلح قد يكون عن إقرار، وقد يقال: وجه المناسبة: أن الإقرار يحصل به قطع المنازعة كما يحصل بالصلح. (فتح) قال في "البحر الرائق": وسببه سبب المعاملات تعلق المقدور بتعاطيه وركنه الإيجاب والقبول الموضوعان له، وشرطه: كون المصالح عليه معلوماً إن كان يحتاج إلى قبضه، والمصالح عنه حقا يجوز الاعتياض عنه ولو على غير مال كالقصاص معلوما كان أو مجهولا لا ما لا يجوز الاعتياض عنه كحق الشفعة وحد القذف والكفالة بالنفس، وطلب الصلح كاف عن القبول من المدعى عليه إن كان المدعى به مما لا يتعين بالتعين، وإن كان مما يتعين فلابد من قبول المدعى عليه ويشترط شرائط ذلك العقد الملحق به من بيع وإجارة. وحكمه في جانب المصالح عليه: وقوع الملك فيه للمدعي، سواء كان المدعى عليه مقرا أو منكرا وفي المصالح عنه: وقوع الملك فيه للمدعى عليه إن كان مما يحتمل التمليك كالمال وكان المدعى عليه مقرا به، وإن كان مما لا يحتمل التمليك كالقصاص وقوع البراءة، كما إذا كان منكرا مطلقاً، والجهالة فيه إن كانت تفضي إلى المنازعة كوقوعها فيما يحتاج إلى التسليم منعت صحته، وإلا لا، فبطل إن كان المصالح عليه أو عنه مجهولا يحتاج إلى التسليم كصلحه بعد دعواه مجهولا على أن يدفع له مالا ولم يسمه.
يرفع النزاع إلخ: أي بين المدعي والمدعى عليه، وركنه الإيجاب والقبول وشرطه: أن يكون البدل أي المصالح عليه مالاً معلوماً إن احتيج إلى قبضه وإلا لا يشترط معلوميته، فإن من ادعى حقاً في دار وادعى المدعى عليه قبله حقاً حانوته، فتصالحا أن يترك كل واحد منهما دعواه قبل صاحبه، صح، وإن لم يبين كل واحد
منهما مقدار حقه؛ لأن جهالة ساقط لا يفضي إلى المنازعة. (شرح إلياس) بإقرار وسكوت إلخ [ أي لا يقر المدعى عليه ولا ينكر. (إلياس)] لإطلاق قوله عليه: "كل صلح جائز بين المسلمين إلا صلحاً أحل حراماً أو حرم حلالاً، أخرجه أبو داود، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز مع الإنكار والسكوت؛ لأنهما صلح أحل حراماً؛ لأنه أخذ المال بغير حق في زعم المدعى عليه، فكان رشوة، ولنا: ما قلنا، ومعنى قوله: "أحل حراماً أو حرم حلالاً أي لعينه، كما إذا صالح على ترك وطء الضرة، أو على أن لا يتصرف في بدل الصلح، أو أن يجعل عوض الصلح خمراً أو خنزيراً [ رمز الحقائق: ۲۲۹/۲] وقوله: أخذ المال بغير حق فكان رشوة غير مسلم؛ لأنه في زعم المدعي عين حقه أو بدله، فهو حلال أخذه، وفي زعم المدعى عليه؛ لافتداء اليمين ودفع الشر عن نفسه، ثم المراد من جواز الصلح اعتباره في إثبات ملك المدعي في بدل الصلح، وانقطاع حق الاسترداد للمدعى عليه، وبطلان حق المدعي في أصل الدعوى. (عيني، فتح، بتصرف من المحشي)
Book of Sulh (Compromise). Definition of Sulh and its Types. Book of Sulh: It is a contract that removes dispute, and it is permissible with acknowledgment and silence. Meaning: sulh in Shariah. Meaning: sulh, i.e., with acknowledgment of the defendant. Book of Sulh: derived from musalaha (reconciliation), opposite of dispute. (Mulla Miskin) Its connection to the previous (book of Iqrar) is that sulh may be based on acknowledgment; and it is said: the connection is that acknowledgment achieves cessation of dispute just as sulh does. (Fath) In al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Its cause is the cause of transactions: the ability to engage in it. Its pillar is offer and acceptance specifically for it. Its condition: that the subject of settlement (al-musalah 'alayhi) be known if it requires delivery, and the right settled (al-musalah 'anhu) must be a right that permits compensation, even for non-property like qiṣāṣ (retribution), whether known or unknown, but not a right that does not permit compensation, such as the right of pre-emption, the ḥadd punishment for slander, and guaranty of person. A request for sulh suffices as acceptance from the defendant if the claim is not specifically determined; if it is specific, the defendant's acceptance is necessary. The conditions of the contract to which it is appended, like sale or lease, also apply. Its ruling regarding the party with whom settlement is made: ownership of the settlement object vests in the plaintiff, whether the defendant acknowledges or denies. Regarding the matter settled: ownership vests in the defendant if it is property and the defendant acknowledged it; if it is not property like qiṣāṣ, then the right is dropped. Ignorance (jahl) in the settlement, if it leads to dispute (as when delivery is needed), prevents validity; otherwise not. So the settlement is void if the settlement object or the subject matter is unknown and requires delivery, like where one claims an unknown amount and settles for an unspecified payment. (The phrase) "removes dispute" etc.: i.e., between plaintiff and defendant. Its pillar is offer and acceptance. Its condition: that the alternative (badal), i.e., the settlement object, be known property if delivery is needed; otherwise knowledge is not required. For example, if one claims a right in a house and the defendant claims a right in his shop, and they settle by each dropping his claim against the other, it is valid even if each does not specify the amount of his right, because ignorance of a dropped claim does not lead to dispute. (Sharh Ilyas) "With acknowledgment and silence" etc.: i.e., the defendant neither acknowledges nor denies. (Ilyas) Due to the generality of his ﷺ statement: "Every sulh is permissible among Muslims except a sulh that makes the unlawful lawful or the lawful unlawful" (Abu Dawud). Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible with denial and silence, because it is a sulh that makes the unlawful lawful, because the plaintiff takes property without right in the defendant's view, so it is bribery. Our proof is what we said. The meaning of his ﷺ statement "makes the unlawful lawful or the lawful unlawful" concerns specifically unlawful things, e.g., settling to abandon intercourse with a co-wife, or to not dispose of the settlement object, or to make the settlement consideration wine or pork [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/229]. His statement "taking property without right, so it is bribery" is not accepted, because in the plaintiff's view it is his exact right or its substitute, so taking it is lawful; in the defendant's view, it is to redeem himself from the oath and repel evil from himself. Then the purpose of sulh's validity is considered in establishing the plaintiff's ownership of the settlement object, cutting off the defendant's right of recovery, and nullifying the plaintiff's right to the original claim. ('Ayni, Fath, with adaptation from the commentator)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage from the beginning of Kitab al-Sulh defines the contract of compromise (sulh) as a binding agreement to end disputes. The Hanafi position is that sulh is valid in three scenarios: when the defendant admits the claim, when he denies it, or when he remains silent. This is based on the general permissibility of sulh in the hadith from Abu Dawud, with the exception only of settlements that involve making the unlawful lawful or vice versa. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees for cases of denial and silence, arguing that it amounts to bribery—taking property without right from the defendant's perspective. The Hanafi response rebuts this: from the plaintiff's perspective, he is taking what he believes is his right or its substitute; from the defendant's perspective, he is paying to avoid an oath and litigation. The text also outlines essential conditions: the settlement object must be specified if it requires delivery; the right being settled must be one that permits compensation (e.g., property, qisas) as opposed to rights like pre-emption, hadd penalty, or personal guaranty. Ignorance that leads to further dispute invalidates the contract, but ignorance of a dropped claim does not harm. The ruling is that the plaintiff becomes owner of the settlement object, the defendant is freed from further claim, and the original claim is extinguished.

Key Terms
الصلح (al-sulh): A contract to end a dispute between two parties, involving a compromise.
المصالح عليه (al-musalah 'alayhi): The object or consideration given to the plaintiff in settlement.
المصالح عنه (al-musalah 'anhu): The right or claim being settled, often a disputed right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is sulh (compromise) invalid?
A) When the defendant denies the claim.
B) When the defendant remains silent.
C) When the settlement involves making the unlawful lawful, e.g., by including wine as compensation.
D) When neither party specifies the exact amount of their claim.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits sulh (compromise) even when the defendant denies or remains silent, based on the general permissibility in the hadith, and distinguishes it from bribery by considering each party's perspective.

Sulh with Denial or Silence: The Shafi'i Objection and Hanafi Rebuttal
Complete inter-madhhab dispute: Shafi'i objection and Hanafi rebuttal on sulh with denial/silence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Shafi'i objection to sulh with denial/silence and state the Hanafi rebuttal, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A sulh paid under denial is not bribery—the plaintiff sees his right, the defendant ransoms his oath.

The validity of a compromise (sulh) when the defendant flatly denies the claim has been a point of sharp disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. Al-Shafi'i argues that such a payment is nothing but bribery, because from the defendant's perspective the plaintiff has no right. The Hanafis respond by examining the intention of each party: the plaintiff believes he is taking his right, and the defendant pays to avoid an oath and litigation. This lesson unpacks the arguments and shows why the Hanafi view ultimately prevails within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that sulh with inkar or sukut is valid. The basis is the general hadith 'كل صلح جائز بين المسلمين' and the fact that each party has a reason: the plaintiff believes he is taking his right or its substitute; the defendant pays to avoid an oath and harm.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that sulh with denial is invalid because it involves taking property without right from the defendant's perspective, thus constituting bribery (رشوة) and falling under the prohibited sulh that makes halal what is haram.
The Shafi'i rely on the hadith that prohibits sulh that makes lawful what is unlawful.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis rebut by clarifying that the prohibition in the hadith applies only to specific objects (like wine or pork) or to sulh that explicitly legalizes a haram act. The general exchange of property in a dispute is not bribery because the plaintiff's view is that the money is his right, and the defendant's payment is to ransom himself from the oath (iftida' al-yamin).
The Hanafis deconstruct the meaning of 'makes lawful what is unlawful'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Hanafi law, a sulh concluded without admission is valid and transfers ownership of the substitute to the plaintiff, while the defendant forfeits any right to reclaim and the plaintiff's original claim is extinguished. Shafi'is require some form of admission or acknowledgment.
This difference affects many everyday dispute settlements.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
Within the Hanafi school, the ruling that sulh with inkar and sukut is valid is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). This is based on the strength of the general hadith and the rational rebuttal of the bribery charge.
Later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani and Ibn Abidin affirm this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز مع الإنكار والسكوت؛ لأنهما صلح أحل حراماً؛ لأنه أخذ المال بغير حق في زعم المدعى عليه، فكان رشوة، ولنا: ما قلنا، ومعنى قوله: "أحل حراماً أو حرم حلالاً أي لعينه، كما إذا صالح على ترك وطء الضرة، أو على أن لا يتصرف في بدل الصلح، أو أن يجعل عوض الصلح خمراً أو خنزيراً [ رمز الحقائق: ۲۲۹/۲] وقوله: أخذ المال بغير حق فكان رشوة غير مسلم؛ لأنه في زعم المدعي عين حقه أو بدله، فهو حلال أخذه، وفي زعم المدعى عليه؛ لافتداء اليمين ودفع الشر عن نفسه، ثم المراد من جواز الصلح اعتباره في إثبات ملك المدعي في بدل الصلح، وانقطاع حق الاسترداد للمدعى عليه، وبطلان حق المدعي في أصل الدعوى. (عيني، فتح، بتصرف من المحشي)
And al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible with denial and silence, because these two are a sulh that makes lawful what is unlawful, because it is taking property without right in the view of the defendant, so it is bribery. And we [Hanafis] have what we stated. And the meaning of his statement: "makes lawful what is unlawful or makes unlawful what is lawful" means concerning the specific object, like when one makes sulh on leaving intercourse with a co-wife, or on not disposing of the substitute, or on making the compensation wine or pig. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/229] And his statement: taking property without right so it is bribery is not accepted, because in the view of the plaintiff it is his right or its substitute, so it is lawful for him to take it, and in the view of the defendant it is to ransom himself from the oath and to repel harm from himself. Then the meaning of the permissibility of sulh is considering it in establishing the plaintiff's ownership of the substitute, and the cutting off of the defendant's right to reclaim, and the nullification of the plaintiff's right in the original claim. (Ayni, Fath, adapted from the marginalia)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage records a complete inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of sulh when the defendant denies the claim (إنكار) or remains silent (سكوت). Al-Shafi'i argues that such sulh is not permissible because it involves taking property without right from the defendant's perspective, making it akin to bribery (رشوة), and thus falls under the prohibited sulh that makes halal what is haram. The Hanafi response (لنا: ما قلنا) refers to the earlier proof from the hadith and emphasizes that the exception in the hadith ('makes lawful what is unlawful') applies only to specific objects that are inherently unlawful, like wine or pork, not to the generic exchange of property in a dispute. The Hanafis refute the charge of bribery: from the plaintiff's perspective, he is taking either his own right or its substitute, so it is halal; from the defendant's perspective, he pays to avoid an oath and to repel harm, which is legitimate. The purpose of sulh is to establish the plaintiff's ownership of the substitute, cut off the defendant's right to reclaim, and nullify the plaintiff's original claim. Thus, the Hanafis maintain that sulh is permissible even without admission.

Key Terms
إنكار (inkar): Denial by the defendant of the plaintiff's claim.
رشوة (rashwah): Bribe; the Shafi'i claim that payment without admission constitutes bribery.
افتداء اليمين (iftida' al-yamin): Ransoming oneself from the oath (i.e., paying to avoid being sworn).
سكوت (sukut): Silence by the defendant (instead of denial or admission).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Shafi'i objection to sulh with denial of the claim?
A) It is not permissible because it involves taking property without right, resembling bribery.
B) It is not permissible because the hadith only allows sulh with admission.
C) It is permissible only if the defendant admits later.
D) It is permissible if the substitute is known.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates sulh even when the defendant denies the claim, because the payment is seen as the plaintiff's right or substitute and the defendant's ransom from an oath, not as bribery.

Sulh as a Sale: When Settlement Becomes a Sale
Expands on the sale-like consequences of sulh when property is exchanged with admission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which sulh is considered a sale, list the sale-derived rights that arise, and distinguish between ignorance of the substitute and ignorance of the claim.

Core Idea
Sulh with property and admission is a sale – ignorance of the substitute invalidates, but ignorance of the claim does not.

This passage explains that when a settlement (sulh) involves property for property with the defendant's admission, the Hanafi school treats it as a sale. As a result, various sale-related rights come into play: preemption, return for defect, and contractual options. However, ignorance of the substitute (badal) invalidates the settlement, whereas ignorance of the original claim (musalah 'anhu) does not. Understanding this distinction is crucial both for drafting valid settlements and for knowing when secondary rights such as preemption apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger condition
The passage begins by stating the condition: if sulh occurs 'for property with property with admission' (عن مال بمال بإقرار), it is considered a sale. Your first step is to recognize that both elements – a property-for-property exchange and the defendant's admission – are necessary.
Without admission, the sulh remains a pure settlement and does not trigger sale rulings.
2
List the sale-derived rights that are established
The text enumerates the rights that now apply: preemption (shuf'a) if the substitute is real estate, return for defect (radd bi al-ayb), option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'ya), and option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart). Your task is to memorize these four rights and understand why they are attached.
These rights exist because the sulh is, in effect, a sale, and the two parties voluntarily exchange property.
3
Recognize what invalidates the sulh
The key invalidator is ignorance (jahala) of the substitute (badal). Since the sulh is a sale, the substitute must be known and capable of delivery. Ignorance of the term (if deferred) or inability to deliver also invalidates. In contrast, ignorance of the original claim (musalah 'anhu) does not harm, because the claim is not being delivered.
This distinction is crucial: badal must be known; musalah anhu may be unknown.
4
Note the interschool difference
The commentary explicitly mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: he does not consider such sulh as a sale. This difference affects practical outcomes, such as whether a neighbor can claim preemption. Be aware of the ikhtilaf and its thamara (consequence).
Al-Shafi'i treats sulh as a sui generis contract, not analogous to sale.

Source Text

أحكام الصلح كتاب الصلح وإنكار، فإن وقع عن مال بمال بإقرار اعتبر بيعا، فيثبت فيه الشفعة والرد بالعيب أي إذا كان بدل الصلح عقارا وخيار الرؤية والشرط، وتفسده جهالة البدل لا جهالة المصالح عنه، وإن استحق بعض المصالح عنه أو كله، أي وخيار الشرط . في الصلح عن إقرار وإنكار إلخ فلو أنكر ثم صالح ثم أقر ، لا يلزمه ما أقر به، وكذا لو أقام بينة بعد صلحه، لا تقبل، ولو أقام بينة على إقرار المدعي أنه لا حق له قبله قبل الصلح أو قبل القبض، والصلح بعد الحلف لا يصح كالصلح مع المودع بعد دعوى الاستهلاك، وصلح الأب عن مال الصبي جائز كيفما كان إن لم يكن له بينة، وإلا لا. [البحر الرائق: ٣٦٥/٧] اعتبر بيعا: [ أي يجري فيه أحكام البيع لوقوع المبادلة بين المالين في حق المتصالحين بترا ضيهما، قال في "البحر الرائق" [٣٦٥/٧] إن كان على خلاف الجنس إلا في مسألتين: الأولى : إذا صالح من الدين على عبد وصاحبه مقر بالدين وقبض العبد ليس له المرابحة من غير بيان الثانية: إذا تصادقا على أن لا دين، بطل الصلح، كما لو استوفى عين حقه، ثم تصادقا أن لا دين فلو تصادقا على أن لا دين لا يبطل الشراء وإن وقع على جنسه، فإن كان أقل من المدعى، فهو حط وإبراء، وإن كان بمثله، فهو قبض واستيفاء، وإن كان بأكثر فهو ربا، وإذا اعتبر بيعاً ثبت أحكامه. فيثبت فيه إلخ: هذا هو تفريع على كون الصلح عن مال بمال بإقرار بيعاً، وبيان فائدة كونه بيعا أي لما كان هذا الصلح بيعاً يثبت فيه أي في هذه الصلح الشفعة إذا كان عقاراً بأن كانت الدعوى في دار في يد رجل قد أقر له بها، فصالح المدعي على مال معين دفعه إليه، فهذا في المعنى بيع وللجار أن يطلب الشفعة فيه، وكذلك يثبت له الرد بالعيب بأن كان بدل الصلح عبداً مثلاً، فوجد المدعي فيه عيباً، له أن يرده؛ لأنه اعتبر بيعاً، وكذا يثبت خيار الرؤية بأن لم ير المصالح ما وقع عليه الصلح وقت الصلح ثم رآه، له الخيار فيه كما في شراء ما لم يره، وخيار الشرط بأن تصالحا على شيء، فشرط أحدهما الخيار لنفسه؛ لأنه من أحكام البيع. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٢٩/٢] وتفسده إلخ: معطوف على قوله: "يثبت"، وبيان لفائدة كون هذا الصلح بيعاً أيضاً أي يفسد الصلح؛ لجهالة البدل مثل: أن يكون البدل عبداً أو دابة؛ لأن جهالة البدل مفضية إلى المنازعة (إلياس) وقال في "الفتح": أي الذي وقع عليه الصلح؛ لأنه بيع فصار كجهالة الثمن [ رمز الحقائق: ۲۲۹/۲] ويشترط القدرة على تسليم البدل. (درر) وكذا يفسد بجهالة الأجل إذا كان البدل مؤجلاً . (زيلعي) البدل بأن يصالح على شيء غير معين وغير مقدر. جهالة إلخ: أي لا يفسده جهالة المصالح عنه؛ لأنه لا يحتاج فيه إلى تسليمه، فلا يضر الجهالة، بخلاف بدل الصلح؛ فإنه يحتاج فيه إلى تسليمه، وفيه خلاف الشافعي له. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٢٩/٢]
Rulings of Sulh. The Book of Sulh and denial: if it occurs for property with property with admission, it is considered a sale, so preemption and option for defect are established in it, i.e., if the substitute is real estate, and option of inspection and stipulation, and ignorance of the substitute invalidates it, not ignorance of the matter being settled, even if some or all of the matter being settled is reclaimed. i.e., option of stipulation. In sulh based on admission and denial etc.: if he denied then made sulh then admitted, he is not bound by what he admitted; likewise if he presents evidence after his sulh, it is not accepted. If he presents evidence that the plaintiff admitted that he has no right against him before the sulh or before taking possession, and sulh after oath is not valid, like sulh with a depositary after claim of consumption. The father's sulh regarding the property of a minor is permissible however it may be if he has no evidence, otherwise not. [al-Bahr al-Raiq: 7/365] Considered a sale: [i.e., the rulings of sale apply to it due to the exchange of property between the two parties with their mutual consent. He said in al-Bahr al-Raiq [7/365]: if it is of a different genus, except in two issues: first: if he settles from a debt for a slave and the debtor admits the debt, and he takes possession of the slave, he does not have the option of profit without clarification. Second: if they both agree that there is no debt, the sulh is invalid, just as if he collected his exact right then they both agree there is no debt; if they agree there is no debt, it does not invalidate the purchase. If it is less than the claim, it is reduction and release; if equal, it is receipt and collection; if more, it is usury. And when it is considered a sale, its rulings are established. So there is established in it etc.: This is a branch on the rule that sulh for property with property with admission is a sale, and an explanation of the benefit of it being a sale. That is, when this sulh is a sale, preemption is established in it if it is real estate, as when the claim is regarding a house in the possession of a man who admitted it to him, so the plaintiff settled for a specific property paid to him; this is a sale in meaning, and the neighbor may claim preemption in it. Likewise, the right of return for defect is established, e.g., if the substitute is a slave and the plaintiff finds a defect, he may return it because it is considered a sale. Likewise, option of inspection is established if the person making sulh did not see the subject of sulh at the time of sulh and then saw it; he has the option as in purchasing what one has not seen. And option of stipulation: if they make sulh on something and one of them stipulates an option for himself, because it is from the rulings of sale. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/229] And ignorance invalidates it etc.: This is connected to his saying "establishes" and an explanation of the benefit of this sulh being a sale as well. That is, the sulh is invalidated by ignorance of the substitute, such as when the substitute is a slave or animal, because ignorance of the substitute leads to dispute. (Ilyas) And it is said in al-Fath: i.e., the subject of sulh, because it is a sale, so it becomes like ignorance of the price. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/229] And ability to deliver the substitute is required. (Durar) Likewise, it is invalidated by ignorance of the term if the substitute is deferred. (Zayla'i) The substitute: by making sulh on something unspecified and unquantified. Ignorance etc.: i.e., ignorance of the matter being settled (musalah anhu) does not invalidate it because it does not require delivery, so ignorance does not harm, unlike the substitute (badal) which requires delivery. And there is a difference of opinion with al-Shafi'i on this. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/229]
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage details the rulings that apply when sulh is treated as a sale (بيع). The matn states that if sulh involves property-for-property (مال بمال) with the defendant's admission (إقرار), it is considered a sale. Consequently, several sale-related rights are established: (1) الشفعة (preemption) if the substitute is real estate, meaning a neighbor or partner can claim preemption; (2) الرد بالعيب (return due to defect) allowing the plaintiff to return a defective substitute; (3) خيار الرؤية (option of inspection) if the subject matter was unseen at the time of contract; and (4) خيار الشرط (stipulated option) if agreed. Ignorance of the substitute (جهالة البدل) invalidates the sulh because, like a sale, the price must be known. However, ignorance of the original claim (المصالح عنه) does not invalidate the settlement, since it does not require delivery. The commentary elaborates on additional details: if a party denies then settles then admits, his admission post-settlement is not binding; evidence after sulh is not accepted; sulh after an oath is invalid; a father may settle for a minor's property if he lacks evidence. The text also addresses scenarios where the settlement is of a different genus than the claim, with two exceptions regarding profit and agreement of no debt. The distinction between ignorance of the substitute (invalid when delivery needed) and ignorance of the claim (harmless) is crucial, and it is noted that al-Shafi'i differs on this last point.

Key Terms
بدل الصلح (badal al-sulh): The property given as substitute in the settlement; its knowledge is required if delivery is needed.
المصالح عنه (al-musalah 'anhu): The original claim or right being settled; ignorance of it is tolerated because it does not require delivery.
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Preemption right of a neighbor or partner to buy the property in a sale; applies to sulh treated as a sale.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option to rescind upon seeing the object of sale if it was unseen at contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is sulh (settlement) considered a sale in the Hanafi school?
A) When it involves property for property with the defendant's denial.
B) When it involves property for property with the defendant's admission.
C) When it involves a property for a debt.
D) Only when the claim is for real estate.

Key Takeaway
Sulh with property and admission is legally a sale, triggering preemption, defect rights, and options; ignorance of the substitute invalidates, but ignorance of the claim does not.

Sulh with Silence or Denial: Dual Nature and Practical Consequences
Ruling on sulh with silence/denial and its dual characterization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the dual legal classification of sulh with silence/denial (fida for denier, mu'awada for claimant) and apply its practical consequences regarding shuf'a, death, and acknowledgment.

Core Idea
In sulh based on silence or denial, the transaction is a ransom for the denier and a sale for the claimant — each judged by his own belief.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on compromise (sulh) when the defendant remains silent or denies the claim outright. Unlike sulh based on acknowledgment, this form of compromise carries a dual legal nature: it is a 'ransom for the oath' (fida' al-yamin) from the denier's perspective and a commutative contract (mu'awada) from the claimant's perspective. This classification, rooted in the parties' subjective beliefs, determines critical practical outcomes such as the applicability of pre-emption (shuf'a), the effect of death, and the validity of embedded acknowledgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its dual classification
The passage states that sulh over silence/denial is a 'fida' (ransom) for the denier (to avoid oath) and a 'mu'awada' (commutative contract) for the claimant (as substitute for claimed right).
This is the core legal concept; all subsequent rulings derive from it.
2
Trace the legal reason (ta'lil) for dual classification
The dual nature arises because each party acts according to his own belief: the denier pays to avoid swearing; the claimant accepts as compensation for his right. The text uses analogies of iqala (cancellation) and marriage to show a single contract can have different rulings for different parties.
This is a key example of Hanafi istihsan and consideration of intention.
3
Derive the first consequence: no shuf'a (pre-emption) for denier
Since from the denier's perspective the transaction is not a sale (but a ransom), the property he pays is not considered sold, so no shuf'a arises for his co-owners or neighbours.
Shuf'a only applies to sales, not to ransoms.
4
Examine the second consequence: effect of death on the contract
The text distinguishes between things that do not vary (like house residence or slave service) and things that vary (like riding animal or wearing clothes). If the claimant dies, the contract remains valid for the former (heir steps in) but annulled for the latter. If the defendant dies, the contract remains entirely.
This mirrors the earlier rules for sulh with acknowledgment but now applies to silence/denial.
5
Analyze the third consequence: effect of killing the slave (intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf)
Muhammad holds the sulh is annulled absolutely if the slave is killed (like ijarah). Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if claimant or stranger kills, a substitute is bought and service continues (with option for claimant); if defendant kills, annulment by consensus.
This is a furu' branching from the dual nature: from claimant's perspective it is a hire-like service, from denier's a ransom.
6
Understand the note on acknowledgment within sulh
If the sulh is annulled, the claimant's prior acknowledgment (that he has no right) is also annulled, but the defendant's acknowledgment (that the property belongs to claimant) remains valid. This is because the defendant's acknowledgment is against his own interest and not contingent on the sulh's validity.
Important for litigation strategy and effect of void compromises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصلح عن سكوت وإنكار فداء لليمين في حق المنكر، ومعاوضة في حق المدعي، وعوض عنه فلا شفعة إن صالح عن دار بهما، بالإنكار والسكوت
وإن مات المدعي فكذلك في خدمة العبد وسكنى الدار؛ إذ الوارث يقوم مقامه فيهما، ويبطل فيما يتفاوت فيه كركوب الدابة ولبس الثوب؛ لأن الصلح لقطع المنازعة وفي إبطاله بموت أحدهما إعادة المنازعة، فبقي فيما لا يتفاوت الناس فيه كخدمة العبد وسكنى الدار، وبطل فيما يتفاوت فيه كركوب الدابة ولبس الثياب، وإن مات المدعى عليه يبقى الصلح وإن مات المدعي يبطل؛ لتعذر إقامة الوارث مقامه وإن قتل العبد يبطل الصلح عند محمد حله مطلقاً كالإجارة، وعند أبي يوسف ليه ينظر، فإن قتله المدعي أو الأجنبي، يضمن قيمته، ويشتري بقيمته عبداً فيخدمه، ولكن يثبت له الخيار، وإن قتله المدعى عليه، يبطل بالإجماع، كما إذا مات حتف أنفه أو أعتقه المولى. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٠/٢]

وقال في "الفتح": إذا بطل الصلح بطل ما في ضمنه من الإقرار الصادر من مدع أو مدعى عليه، كذا قيل معزياً للحموي، وأقول : عبارة الحموي عن "القنية" بخطه: إذا أقر المدعي في ضمن الصلح أنه لا حق له في هذا الشيء، ثم بطل الصلح، يبطل إقراره الذي كان في ضمنه وله أن يدعيه بعد ذلك، والمدعى عليه إذا أقر عند الصلح بأن هذا الشيء للمدعي، ثم بطل الصلح، فإنه يرد ذلك الشيء إلى المدعي انتهى فهي صريحة في أن إقرار المدعى عليه في ضمن الصلح لا يبطل ببطلانه، فتنبه. والصلح عن سكوت إلخ: لما فرغ المصنف من بيان مسائل الصلح مع إقرار، وهو أحد الأقسام الثلاثة للصلح، شرع في مسائل القسمين الآخرين أي الصلح مع سكوت وإنكار. حبيب الرحمن فداء لليمين إلخ: لأنه في زعمه أن لا حق عليه، وأن المدعي مبطل في دعواه، وإنما دفع المال إليه لئلا يحلف ويقطع الخصومة. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٠/٢] و معاوضة إلخ : أي الصلح عن سكوت وإنكار معاوضة في حق المدعي، فبطل الصلح على دراهم بعد دعوى دراهم إذا تفرقا قبل القبض، ووجه كونه معاوضة: أن المدعي يزعم أنه يأخذه عوضاً عن ماله، وأنه محق في دعواه، ويجوز أن يكون في شيء واحد حكمان مختلفان باعتبار شخصين كالنكاح موجبه الحل في المتناكحين، والحرمة في أصولهما، فيؤاخذ كل واحد منهما بما زعم رمز الحقائق: ۲۳۰/۲] وقال في "العناية" في هذا المقام: لما بينا أن المدعي يأخذه عوضاً في زعمه، فإن قيل: العقد لما اتصف بصفة كيف يتصف بصفة أخرى تقابلها؟ أجاب بقوله : ويجوز أن يختلف حكم العقد في حقهما كما يختلف حكم الإقالة فإنها فسخ في حق المتعاقدين بيع جديد في حق ثالث وكعقد النكاح فإن حكمه الحل في حق امرأته والتحريم المؤبد في أمها. فلا شفعة إلخ: هذا هو تفريع على كون الصلح عن سكوت ،وإنكار فداء لليمين في حق المنكر لا معاوضة، وصورته: ادعى على رجل داراً، فأنكر أو سكت، ثم صالح عنها بدفع شيء آخر، لا يجب في داره أي المنكر الشفعة؛
And the compromise based on silence and denial is a ransom for the oath regarding the denier, and a commutative contract regarding the claimant, and it is a consideration for him, so there is no pre-emption (shuf'a) if he makes a compromise for a house through both (i.e., denial and silence).
And if the claimant dies, it is likewise in the service of the slave and residence of the house, because the heir stands in his place in them. And it is annulled in what varies (among people) such as riding the animal and wearing the garment, because the compromise is to cut off dispute, and in its annulment by the death of one of them is a renewal of dispute. So it remains in what people do not differ in, such as service of the slave and residence of the house, and it is annulled in what they differ in, such as riding the animal and wearing garments. And if the defendant dies, the compromise remains; if the claimant dies, it is annulled because the heir cannot stand in his place. And if the slave is killed, the compromise is annulled according to Muhammad absolutely, like a lease. According to Abu Yusuf, it depends: if the claimant or a stranger kills him, he guarantees his value and buys with the value a slave to serve him, but he has the option; if the defendant kills him, it is annulled by consensus, as if he died naturally or the master emancipated him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 230/2]

And it is said in al-Fath: If the compromise is annulled, what is included in it of the acknowledgment made by the claimant or defendant is annulled. So it is said, attributed to al-Hamawi. And I say: Al-Hamawi's expression from al-Quniyah in his handwriting: If the claimant acknowledges within the compromise that he has no right to this thing, then the compromise is annulled, his acknowledgment that was within it is annulled, and he may claim it afterwards. And if the defendant acknowledges at the time of compromise that this thing belongs to the claimant, then the compromise is annulled, he returns that thing to the claimant. End quote. So it is explicit that the acknowledgment of the defendant within the compromise is not annulled by its annulment, so be mindful.

"And the compromise based on silence etc.": When the author finished explaining issues of compromise with acknowledgment, which is one of three divisions of compromise, he began to explain the issues of the other two divisions, i.e., compromise with silence and denial. (Habib al-Rahman) "Ransom for the oath etc.": because in his (the denier's) belief, there is no right against him or the claimant is false in his claim, and he only pays the money so as not to swear and to cut off the dispute. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 230/2] "And a commutative contract etc.": i.e., compromise based on silence and denial is a commutative contract regarding the claimant. So if the compromise is for dirhams after a claim of dirhams, it becomes invalid if they separate before receipt. And the reason it is a commutative contract is that the claimant believes he is taking it as a substitute for his property and that he is correct in his claim. And it is possible that in one thing there are two different rulings in consideration of two persons, like marriage: its consequence is permissible (halal) between the spouses and forbidden in the spouses' origins (mothers, daughters). Thus, each of them is taken according to what he believes. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 230/2] And it is said in al-Inayah in this place: Since we have explained that the claimant takes it as a substitute in his belief, if it is said: How can a contract having one attribute also have another contradictory attribute? He answered by saying: It is possible that the ruling of the contract differs between two parties, just as the ruling of a cancellation (iqala) differs: it is a rescission regarding the two contractors and a new sale regarding a third party, and like the marriage contract: its ruling is halal regarding his wife and permanent prohibition regarding her mother. "So no pre-emption etc.": This is a branching based on the fact that compromise based on silence and denial is a ransom for the oath regarding the denier, not a commutative contract. Its example: He claimed a house from a man, and he denied or remained silent, then he compromised for it by paying something else. In his (the denier's) house, pre-emption is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage forms the second major section of the chapter on sulh, covering compromise based on silence or denial (sukut wa inkar). The author first establishes a dual characterization: for the denier (the defendant who denies or remains silent), the sulh is a 'fida' (ransom) to avoid taking an oath; for the claimant, it is a 'mu'awada' (commutative contract) because he believes he is receiving a substitute for his right. This dual nature has practical consequences: for example, no pre-emption (shuf'a) applies to the denier's property if he compromises a house claim by paying something else, because the transaction is not a sale from his perspective. The passage then discusses various sub-issues: the effect of death on the compromise (similar to earlier discussion, but now in context of silence/denial), the killing of a slave who is the subject of service, and importantly, the note from al-Fath about the acknowledgment within the compromise: only the claimant's acknowledgment is voided if the compromise is annulled; the defendant's acknowledgment remains binding. The text also cites al-Inayah to justify how a single contract can have two conflicting attributes for different parties, using analogies of iqala and marriage.

Key Terms
فداء اليمين (fida' al-yamin): Ransom for the oath; the denier pays to avoid swearing an oath that he owes nothing.
معاوضة (mu'awada): Commutative contract; a contract where each party gives and receives something of value.
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Pre-emption right; the right of a co-owner to buy out another's share in a property when sold.
الإقالة (al-iqala): Cancellation of a sale; in Hanafi, it is rescission for the parties but a new sale for third parties.
الإجارة (al-ijara): Lease contract; Muhammad likens the service sulh to ijarah for annulment upon destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a compromise based on denial, why is there no pre-emption (shuf'a) for the denier's property?
A) Because the compromise is a gift.
B) Because from the denier's perspective, it is a ransom, not a sale.
C) Because pre-emption is only for real estate sales.
D) Because the compromise is void.

Key Takeaway
Sulh with silence/denial is dual: it is a ransom for the defendant and a commutative contract for the claimant, each affecting different rules such as shuf'a, death, and acknowledgment annulment.

Sulh upon Denial: Dual Nature and Rulings on Death and Slave Killing
Defines sulh upon denial/silence and its rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the dual nature of sulh upon denial (fida' lil yamin for defendant, mu'awada for claimant) and apply its effects on shuf'a, death of parties, and slave killing, distinguishing the views of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Sulh upon denial is a ransom for oath for the defendant and an exchange for the claimant — this dual nature governs shuf'a, inheritance, and slave killing.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq examines the unique fiqh classification of a compromise made when the defendant denies the claim or remains silent. Understanding that from the defendant's perspective it is 'fida' lil yamin' (ransom to avoid oath) and from the claimant's perspective it is 'mu'awada' (exchange) is crucial for predicting legal consequences: whether pre-emption applies, whether the contract survives death of a party, and what happens if the slave subject to the compromise is killed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dual nature
Recognize that sulh upon denial/silence is treated as two different contracts: for the defendant, it is a payment to avoid taking an oath (fida' lil yamin); for the claimant, it is an exchange (mu'awada) where the payment compensates for the claimed right.
This dual nature is the foundation for all subsequent rulings.
2
Apply to shuf'a (pre-emption)
Since the defendant is not selling his property but paying ransom, no right of shuf'a arises on his property. However, if the claimant transfers property as payment, it is a sale from his perspective and pre-emption may apply.
The text explicitly states 'so there is no pre-emption if he compromises concerning a house' — referring to the defendant's property.
3
Analyse the effect of death of the claimant
For non-varying benefits (slave service, house dwelling), the heir steps into the claimant's place and the compromise remains valid. For varying benefits (riding an animal, wearing clothes), the compromise becomes invalid because the benefit cannot be replicated.
The rationale: sulh is to cut off dispute; invalidating it upon death revives the dispute, so it is preserved where possible.
4
Analyse the effect of death of the defendant
If the defendant dies, the compromise remains valid because his obligation passes to his estate; there is no personal reliance on the defendant's oath.
The text affirms: 'if the defendant dies, the compromise remains'.
5
Examine the slave-killing dispute
Muhammad holds the compromise becomes invalid absolutely (like a lease subject matter destroyed). Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if the claimant or a third party kills, the claimant guarantees value and may buy a substitute with an option; if the defendant kills, invalidation by consensus.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the matn presents Muhammad's view as the relied position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصلح عن سكوت وإنكار فداء لليمين في حق المنكر، ومعاوضة في حق المدعي، وعوض عنه فلا شفعة إن صالح عن دار بهما، وإن مات المدعي فكذلك في خدمة العبد وسكنى الدار؛ إذ الوارث يقوم مقامه فيهما، ويبطل فيما يتفاوت فيه كركوب الدابة ولبس الثوب؛ لأن الصلح لقطع المنازعة وفي إبطاله بموت أحدهما إعادة المنازعة، فبقي فيما لا يتفاوت الناس فيه كخدمة العبد وسكنى الدار، وبطل فيما يتفاوت فيه كركوب الدابة ولبس الثياب، وإن مات المدعى عليه يبقى الصلح وإن مات المدعي يبطل؛ لتعذر إقامة الوارث مقامه وإن قتل العبد يبطل الصلح عند محمد حله مطلقاً كالإجارة، وعند أبي يوسف ليه ينظر، فإن قتله المدعي أو الأجنبي، يضمن قيمته، ويشتري بقيمته عبداً فيخدمه، ولكن يثبت له الخيار، وإن قتله المدعى عليه، يبطل بالإجماع، كما إذا مات حتف أنفه أو أعتقه المولى. رمز الحقائق: ٢٣٠/٢]
And compromise [sulh] upon silence and denial is a ransom for the oath in the right of the denier, and an exchange in the right of the claimant, and compensation from him (meaning the defendant), so there is no pre-emption if he compromises concerning a house with both (i.e., denial and silence). And if the claimant dies, similarly in the service of the slave and dwelling in the house, because the heir stands in his place in both, and it becomes invalid in what varies among people, like riding an animal and wearing a garment, because compromise is for cutting off dispute, and invalidating it upon the death of one of them revives the dispute, so it remains in what people do not vary in, like service of the slave and dwelling in the house, and becomes invalid in what varies, like riding an animal and wearing clothes. And if the defendant dies, the compromise remains; if the claimant dies, it becomes invalid, because it is impossible for the heir to stand in his place. And if the slave is killed, the compromise becomes invalid according to Muhammad, absolutely, like lease, and according to Abu Yusuf, he has a view: if the claimant or a third party kills him, he guarantees its value, and buys a slave with its value to serve him, but he has the option; if the defendant kills him, it becomes invalid by consensus, as if it died by itself or the master freed it. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 230/2]
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, explaining the legal nature of sulh (compromise) when it occurs upon the defendant's denial or silence (sukut wa inkar). The author clarifies that from the defendant's perspective, the payment made to the plaintiff is considered a 'ransom to avoid the oath' (fida' lil yamin), because the defendant denies any liability and pays only to prevent the plaintiff from taking an oath and to end the dispute. From the plaintiff's perspective, it is an exchange (mu'awada), because he takes the payment as compensation for his claimed right. Consequently, if the compromise involves a house, no right of pre-emption (shuf'a) arises for the defendant's property, because it is not a sale from his viewpoint. However, if the compromise is made by transferring a house as payment, pre-emption is established (as will be explained later). The passage then discusses the effect of death of either party or the killing of the slave who is the subject of the compromise. If the claimant dies, the compromise remains valid for continuous, non-varying benefits like slave service and house dwelling, because the heir can step in; but for varying benefits like riding an animal or wearing clothes, it becomes invalid because the heir cannot replicate the exact benefit. If the defendant dies, the compromise remains valid because the obligation to pay passes to his estate. If the claimant dies, the compromise becomes invalid because the oath-fiduciary purpose is personal to the claimant. Regarding the slave: if the slave is killed, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Muhammad holds the compromise is absolutely invalidated, like in a lease (ijara). Imam Abu Yusuf distinguishes: if the claimant or a stranger kills, the claimant guarantees the value and must buy a slave with it to serve, but he has the option to invalidate the compromise; if the defendant kills, the compromise is invalid by consensus, as if the slave died naturally or was freed by his master.

Key Terms
صلح عن سكوت وإنكار (sulh 'an sukūt wa inkār): A compromise made without the defendant admitting the claim, either by remaining silent or denying.
فداء لليمين (fidā' lil-yamīn): Payment made by the defendant to avoid having to take an oath of denial, since the plaintiff could demand an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In sulh upon denial, if the claimant dies and the benefit is the service of a slave, what happens to the sulh?
A) It becomes invalid immediately.
B) It remains valid because the heir can take the slave's service.
C) It remains valid only if the heir agrees.
D) It becomes invalid and the heir can sue for the original claim.

Key Takeaway
Sulh upon denial is a ransom for oath for the defendant and an exchange for the claimant; this duality dictates the effects on shuf'a, death of parties, and slave killing, and the relied Hanafi position invalidates absolutely when the slave is killed.

Effect of Sulh Invalidity on Acknowledgment
Clarifies whether acknowledgments made within a sulh survive its invalidation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of sulh invalidity on acknowledgments made by the claimant and defendant, and distinguish between the two cases.

Core Idea
The defendant's acknowledgment in sulh stands alone; the claimant's falls with the contract.

This passage resolves a tension between a general statement in al-Fath and a more nuanced view from al-Qunyah. It distinguishes between two parties in a sulh, showing that the defendant's acknowledgment is an independent admission, while the claimant's is conditional. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the rules of sulh properly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general claim
Al-Fath initially states that all acknowledgments within a sulh are invalidated if the sulh is invalidated.
2
Locate the refinement
Al-Hamawi from al-Qunyah distinguishes between claimant and defendant: the claimant's acknowledgment is void, but the defendant's remains valid.
This is quoted in the passage as the correct view.
3
Analyse the distinction
The claimant's acknowledgment is conditional on the sulh's survival; the defendant's is an independent admission of the other's right, not contingent on the sulh.
The defendant's admission is a standalone proof of the claimant's ownership.
4
State the ruling
The mufta bihi position: the defendant's acknowledgment survives the invalidation of the sulh, and he must return the property to the claimant.
The claimant can reassert his claim after the sulh fails.
5
Apply the ruling
In a practical case: if the defendant acknowledged the claimant's right during sulh and the sulh fails, the defendant must still fulfill that acknowledgment.
The acknowledgment is binding independently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في "الفتح": إذا بطل الصلح بطل ما في ضمنه من الإقرار الصادر من مدع أو مدعى عليه، كذا قيل معزياً للحموي، وأقول : عبارة الحموي عن "القنية" بخطه: إذا أقر المدعي في ضمن الصلح أنه لا حق له في هذا الشيء، ثم بطل الصلح، يبطل إقراره الذي كان في ضمنه وله أن يدعيه بعد ذلك، والمدعى عليه إذا أقر عند الصلح بأن هذا الشيء للمدعي، ثم بطل الصلح، فإنه يرد ذلك الشيء إلى المدعي انتهى فهي صريحة في أن إقرار المدعى عليه في ضمن الصلح لا يبطل ببطلانه، فتنبه.
And he said in al-Fath: 'If the sulh becomes invalid, whatever acknowledgment within it from the claimant or defendant becomes invalid.' It was said quoting al-Hamawi, and I say: al-Hamawi's expression from al-Qunyah in his handwriting: 'If the claimant acknowledges within the sulh that he has no right in this thing, then the sulh becomes invalid, his acknowledgment that was within it becomes invalid and he may claim it afterwards. And the defendant, if he acknowledges at the time of sulh that this thing belongs to the claimant, then the sulh becomes invalid, he returns that thing to the claimant.' End quote. It is explicit that the defendant's acknowledgment within the sulh does not become invalid with its invalidation, so beware.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya-like) resolving a seeming contradiction. The commentator from al-Fath initially states that any acknowledgment within a sulh is invalidated if the sulh is invalidated. However, he corrects this by quoting al-Hamawi from al-Qunyah, who distinguishes between the claimant and defendant. If the claimant acknowledges that he has no right (i.e., he admits his claim was false) within the sulh, and then the sulh is invalidated, that acknowledgment is also invalidated, and the claimant can resume his claim. This is because the claimant's acknowledgment was conditioned upon the sulh's survival. But if the defendant acknowledges the claimant's right within the sulh, that acknowledgment survives the invalidation of the sulh; the defendant must return the item to the claimant. The reason is that the defendant's acknowledgment is an independent admission not contingent on the sulh. The commentator ends by warning the reader to note this distinction.

Key Terms
إقرار في ضمن الصلح (iqrār fī ḍimni al-ṣulḥ): An acknowledgment made by either party as part of the settlement agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the defendant in a sulh acknowledges that the disputed property belongs to the claimant, and then the sulh is invalidated, what happens?
A) The acknowledgment is also invalidated.
B) The acknowledgment remains valid and the defendant must return the property.
C) The acknowledgment is valid only if the claimant agrees.
D) The acknowledgment becomes a new contract.

Key Takeaway
The defendant's acknowledgment in a sulh is an independent admission that survives the invalidation of the sulh, while the claimant's acknowledgment is conditional and falls with the sulh.

Pre-emption in Sulh and Return upon Third Party Claim
Ruling on pre-emption in sulh and istihqaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when pre-emption applies in sulh upon denial and explain the process when a third party claims the disputed property.

Core Idea
Pre-emption applies to property received in sulh because it is an exchange in the claimant's view; if the original property is claimed, the substitute must be returned and the lawsuit revives.

This lesson examines two interconnected rulings: the obligation of pre-emption (shuf'a) when a defendant compromises by transferring a house, and the legal effect when a third party (mustahiqq) proves ownership of the originally disputed property. The passage clarifies that, from the claimant's perspective, the compromise is an exchange (mu'awada), thus triggering pre-emption. It also delineates the process for the claimant to return the substitute and resume litigation against the third party.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon. Here, a claimant and defendant reach a sulh (compromise) where the defendant gives a house as compensation for the claimed right. The ruling: pre-emption is wajib for the neighbor against the claimant who receives the house.
The pre-emption is established even if the defendant denies it is an exchange.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof given: the claimant takes the house as compensation for his claimed right, so in his view it is an exchange (mu'awada). This reasoning (talil) is the basis for the ruling.
The dalil is not a scriptural text but a rational inference.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the reasoning lead to pre-emption? Pre-emption is established in sales and exchanges. Since the claimant views the sulh as an exchange, the property acquired through it is subject to pre-emption, analogous to a sale.
The defendant's contrary view does not affect because the ruling is based on the claimant's perspective.
4
Note the exception for third party claim
If a third party proves ownership of the disputed property (the original subject of the claim), the claimant must return the substitute he received and can resume the lawsuit against the third party. If only part is claimed, proportional return and revival occur.
The reason: the claimant abandoned his lawsuit only in exchange for receiving the substitute; if the substitute is lost, his claim revives.
5
Differentiate from formal sale
In a formal sale (bai'), if a third party claims the property, the buyer sues the seller for the property itself, not for the substitute. This contrasts with sulh, where the claimant sues the third party directly.
The difference lies in the nature of the transaction: sale is an explicit exchange, while sulh is originally a compromise to end dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(حبيب) (الرحمن ورد البدل: أي العوض الذي أخذه من مال المدعى عليه، توضيحه: زيد ادعى داراً في يد عمرو، فأنكر عمرو أو سكت، ثم صالح على مائة، فصارت المائة في يد زيد، والدار في يد عمرو، ثم استحق كل الدار، فإن زيداً يرد المائة إلى عمرو، ويرجع بالخصومة في الدار مع لأنه قائم مقام المدعى عليه حين أخذ المدعي منه، فيكون له أن يخاصمه. And it is obligatory if he compromises upon a house with both (denial and silence). And if the disputed property is claimed (by a third party), the claimant returns to the lawsuit. Meaning the pre-emption for the neighbor upon denial or silence. All of it after the sulh and the substitute, and if partly then proportionally. And if the compromise subject or part of it is claimed, it is because he claims that his house is his, and that he retains it as it was, and that what he paid to the claimant is not compensation for it, but only to ransom the oath and cut off the dispute. Then Zayd returns the hundred to Amr and returns to the lawsuit over the house with the claimant because he stands in the place of the defendant when he took from him, so he may litigate with him. Meaning if part of the disputed property is claimed, he returns to the lawsuit and the claimant returns to the defendant proportionally. Its form: if half the house is claimed by a claimant in the mentioned case, Zayd returns fifty to Amr and returns to the claimant in litigation for the half that was claimed. The claimant returns to the lawsuit for all if all the substitute is claimed, or returns to the lawsuit for part if part is claimed, because the claimant did not abandon the lawsuit except that the substitute be delivered to him. So if it is not delivered, he returns to the substituted, which is the lawsuit. Unlike if the compromise occurred with the wording of sale, where one says 'I sold you this thing for this' and the other says 'I bought', where the claimant upon claim (third party) returns against the defendant for the claimed property itself, not the lawsuit, because the defendant's action in entering into the sale is...
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage expands the ruling on pre-emption (shuf'a) in sulh upon denial/silence. The matn states that when the compromise is made by transferring a house (i.e., the defendant pays by giving a house), pre-emption is obligatory for the neighbor against the claimant who receives the house, because from the claimant's perspective this is an exchange (mu'awada) — he takes the house as compensation for his alleged right. Even if the defendant denies it is an exchange, the pre-emption still applies because the claimant's view establishes the exchange for him. The text then discusses the scenario where a third party (mustahiqq) proves ownership of the disputed property. In such a case, the original claimant who received the substitute must return it to the defendant and can resume the lawsuit against the third party. He stands in the defendant's shoes regarding the object. If only part of the property is claimed, he returns part of the substitute and resumes lawsuit for that part. The reason is that the claimant only abandoned his claim in exchange for receiving the substitute; if the substitute is taken away, his claim revives. This differs from a formal sale (sulh with words of sale), where upon third party claim, the claimant directly sues the defendant for the original property because the defendant sold it.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a property transferred in a sale-like transaction.
الصلح (al-sulh): Compromise: a contract to end a dispute by mutual agreement, often involving payment or transfer of property.
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): A third party's claim of ownership over the property that was subject to the compromise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Sue the defendant for the house's value.
D) Do nothing; the third party must sue the defendant.

Key Takeaway
Pre-emption applies to property acquired in sulh as an exchange, and if a third party claims the original property, the claimant returns the substitute and revives the lawsuit.

Shuf'a, Istihqaq, and Halaak in Sulh
Exposition of rulings with qiyas on compromise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on compromise concerning pre-emption, third-party claims, and destruction of the consideration, and derive these rulings using qiyas.

Core Idea
Compromise is treated as a sale for pre-emption; third-party claims or destruction can void or adjust it.

Compromise (sulh) is a common way to settle property disputes. But does it trigger the neighbor's right of pre-emption? What happens if a third party claims the property? This lesson unpacks three key rulings from the Hanafi school, showing how qiyas on sale determines these outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shuf'a ruling in sulh
Determine when pre-emption applies: if a plaintiff and defendant compromise on a house (with denial or silence), the neighbor has the right to pre-empt that house. The plaintiff takes the house as compensation, making it an exchange.
The defendant's denial does not prevent the right.
2
Analyze the qiyas reasoning for shuf'a
The original case (asl) is a sale, where pre-emption applies. The new case (far') is a compromise. The effective cause (illa) is that the plaintiff receives property as compensation (iwad), making it a contract of exchange. Therefore, pre-emption applies to the property received in compromise.
This is qiyas jali with illa of exchange.
3
Examine the effect of third-party claim on the disputed property (istihqaq of the subject matter)
If a third party proves ownership of the original disputed property, the plaintiff returns the consideration he received and resumes litigation against the claimant. This is because the compromise was conditional on the defendant's ownership.
If only part is claimed, the return and litigation are proportional.
4
Examine the effect of third-party claim on the consideration (istihqaq of the badal)
If the consideration itself (e.g., the house given to the plaintiff) is claimed by a third party, the plaintiff returns to his original claim (the compromise is void), unless the consideration is of the same type as the claimed property and not specifically determined.
This preserves the plaintiff's right to his original claim.
5
Examine the effect of destruction (halaak) of the consideration before delivery
If the consideration is destroyed before delivery, the same rule applies as if it were claimed: the compromise is void if the consideration was determinate; if indeterminate (like dirhams), it is not void because the obligation is to deliver the equivalent.
This parallels the rule for sale.
